Current Affairs Commentary

New Crisis Under Confusing Circumstances 6

The recent developments in the Northeast issue, as well as international attitudes, have suddenly become confusing and bewildering. In Japan, rumors are spreading about the renewal of the Tianjin incident and simultaneous uprisings plotted by Japanese in various ports along the river. Troops are pressing toward Jinzhou, and at one point, reinforcements were sent. On the other hand, part of the Japanese army suddenly withdrew within the South Manchuria Railway (SMR) zone. Both Shidehara and the Minister of War and the General Staff expressed that they would not take hostile actions against Jinzhou. Internationally, the League of Nations is everywhere yielding to Japan and complying with its demands, while U.S. Secretary of State Stimson has again issued remarks expressing dissatisfaction with Japan. British public opinion towards Japan is also becoming increasingly intense. In our country, there is much talk domestically about recovering lost territory, while Shi Zhaoji, our representative at the League of Nations, is showing signs of compromising on resolutions. Based on these phenomena, the situations on all sides are extremely contradictory and vague, making us feel as if we are lost in a fog, unable to grasp the true reality of the current situation.

However, it is precisely because the current situations on all sides are confusing and bewildering, making it impossible for us to grasp, that it is necessary for our people to pay close attention to this phenomenon. We believe that the current confusing situation has proven that our country has entered a new and serious period. The persecution by the Japanese in the past has now turned into diplomatic pressure. The encroachment by Japan alone in the past has now turned into a collective effort by various countries to plot against us. The enthusiasm and determination of our country in upholding justice, protecting our national territory, and restraining violence has now gradually diminished. If this conjecture, unfortunately, proves to be correct, then we dare to assert that "the northeastern half of our country will forever change its appearance from now on, with no hope of recovery."

We believe that the reason why a part of the Japanese army suddenly withdrew to within the SMR zone is, on the one hand, to ease the international situation, and on the other hand, to alleviate the resentment of our people. They are retreating to advance, defending to attack, deliberately withdrawing a very small part of their troops to divert the world's attention and achieve their ambition of permanently occupying our Northeast. The reason why the League of Nations does not hesitate to bow down and wholeheartedly suppress us and favor Japan is to establish an extremely ridiculous so-called neutral zone within our territory, to prevent the Japanese army from attacking Jinzhou, in order to maintain its faint existence. It can also use this as an excuse to adjourn the meeting, allowing our country and Japan to negotiate directly. As for the sudden expression of severe intervention by the United States and Britain when the Japanese army pressed westward towards Jinzhou the other day, it was because the area west of Jinzhou was not within the sphere of influence of the Japanese, and the Japanese did not know when to stop, and wanted to advance westward, encroaching on the sphere of influence of other countries. Therefore, Britain and the United States had to use a strong attitude to restrain their excessive expansion of power. This fact is extremely clear. Therefore, the criticism of Japan by Britain and the United States is not out of love for us, but rather a concrete manifestation of their attempt to divide China and seize a piece each. Our people should not feel relieved by the withdrawal of the Japanese army and the assistance of Britain and the United States. It must be known that the lost territory in the Northeast has not yet been recovered. The Japanese army within the SMR zone can still launch an attack at any time. Britain and the United States are by no means sincerely helping us. The day when the League of Nations adjourns will be the time when our country and Japan will directly negotiate. There will be many difficulties in the future, and we must not have any slackness or relief.

Our authorities must never show fear of trouble and retreat before the Northeast is recovered, nor should they make any compromises, lest our Northeast fall into a state of irrecoverable destruction. For at this time, our country has reached a new and serious period. Our people must pay attention to this. Our government must respect public opinion, uphold justice, and fight to the end to protect the life of the nation.

Domestic Important Telegrams Received

Cavalry always aims to defeat the many with the few, not defending strongholds nor attacking hard targets, making the most of its plains combat capabilities. The Provincial Government will not necessarily be located in any fixed place, and it will be determined based on the situation whether to move. The time for a counterattack cannot be predetermined either; it will be launched when the opportunity arises. Even with eyes closed, we can find our way freely in the eastern part of Heilongjiang. Even if the enemy approaches with a hundred or a thousand times our strength, I will not flinch. I am confident that I have the backbone of a man and vow to fight to the end, never becoming a slave of a conquered nation. I have no objection to Fourth Master Zhang taking charge of the administration in Heilongjiang, but if there is even one Japanese person in the provincial capital, I will treat him as an enemy. He may be willing to surrender to Japan, but I cannot betray my responsibility to defend the territory and accept the rule of a conquered nation. According to Fourth Master Zhang, namely Zhang Jinghui (5), future plans are to deploy three lines of defense along the Qiqihar-Keshan line, but adopting mobile cavalry tactics, not sticking to rigid defense, and advancing whenever there is an opportunity. Defense corps will be established in each county, with a lieutenant colonel assigned to every three counties. Each battalion will have four company commanders, and each battalion will consist of five hundred men, all organized as cavalry. They must be formed by December 15th, and I will personally inspect them. (30th Dispatch)

(Tokyo) According to a dispatch from Shenyang, the Japanese military headquarters has heard that General Ma Zhanshan is currently leading troops from Hailun towards Qiqihar,

ready to be mobilized upon orders. If necessary, reinforcements will be sent from Shenyang to Heihe. Further dispatch: The Japanese military headquarters dispatched the main force of a brigade to Qiqihar tonight to prevent Ma's army from counterattacking. (30th Reuters Dispatch)

(Beiping) Ma Zhanshan is currently in Hailun, occasionally visiting Keshan, Bairun, and other places, observing the battle situation. His troops are now concentrated, and reinforcements are arriving continuously. There are about 1,700 Japanese troops in Heilongjiang, and due to fear of the cold, they have shown signs of retreat. (30th Dispatch)

(Beiping) According to people from Bu Kui (Qiqihar), Ma Zhanshan withdrew from Jiangqiao on the 18th, and Heilongjiang fell into a state of anarchy. On the 19th, part of the Japanese army entered the city, the military headquarters, and conducted strict searches of the residences of various important figures. Before leaving Heilongjiang, Ma published a letter to the elders and fathers of Heilongjiang, stating that although he had withdrawn from the provincial capital, he was determined to continue fighting the Japanese to the end with his previous spirit. Ma was stationed in Hailun. On the 23rd, the Japanese army attacked Tai'an and came into contact with our Wu and Fan clans. Ma Qing personally supervised the battle, and about 700 Japanese soldiers were killed in the Huai Shu Gou area. Dōmon, the commander of the Japanese army, sent someone to contact the chamber of commerce, ordering them to make 300 coffins within three days to transport the Japanese soldiers back to the province. The public security of the provincial capital is maintained by the police. The Japanese army, due to the severe cold in Heilongjiang, has no intention of garrisoning for a long time and is preparing to withdraw to southern Manchuria. (30th Dispatch)

Zhang Jinghui 7

Sends Personnel to Take Over Heilongjiang

(Harbin) Ying Shun, the chairman of the committee sent by Zhang Jinghui to take over the Heilongjiang regime, along with committee members Song Wenlin, Zhang Lanjun, Wei Shaozhou, Liu Tingya, Zhang Jingbi, and Li Hanchuan, arrived in Heilongjiang and are scheduled to take over on the 1st. At the same time, the maintenance association established by Heilongjiang gentry and merchants will be abolished. The security team sent by Zhang Jinghui to Heilongjiang was refused armed passage on the Eastern Railway, so one company marched unarmed on the 28th, with weapons transported separately. (30th Dispatch)

(Harbin) Zhao Zhongren telegraphed Ma Zhanshan, asking him to hand over the seal of Heilongjiang Province to Zhang Jinghui. Ma replied that the seal was received from the Central Government, and the transfer must have an order from the Central Government. Now, Zhao has come to Harbin and is making several telephone calls to Hailun every day, intimidating Ma. (30th Dispatch)

(Harbin) On the evening of the 29th, the Japanese army in Heilongjiang opened the Tao'an-Ang'angxi Railway to two thousand people. Currently, there are not many Japanese troops in Heilongjiang. (30th Dispatch)

(Harbin) The Heilongjiang National Salvation Association telegraphed Beijing, requesting punishment for the traitors Zhao Zhongren, Li Wei, Zhou Gaoxiang, and Wan Guobin. (30th Dispatch)

Ma's Troops After Bitter Fighting 8

(Harbin) A reporter went to Hailun on the 27th to investigate and has now returned to Harbin. The current situation of the Heilongjiang army is as follows: The First Brigade, Wan Chonggu's unit, suffered the heaviest casualties. The three regiments now have a strength of three thousand men. Of the nine cannons, three remain. The Eighth Cavalry Brigade, Cheng Zhiyuan's unit, now has a strength of four thousand men. Wu Songshan's brigade now has a strength of three thousand men. The Fourth Regiment of the Guard Regiment, the Third Regiment of Zhang's brigade, the First Regiment of the Third Brigade, the Fifth Regiment, the newly formed replenishment regiment, etc., all have a strength of over a thousand men. Because the gathering points for each brigade and regiment were not in one place during the retreat, it will take some time to gather them, and reorganization will also take a considerable amount of time. The artillery suffered particularly heavy losses, and there is a shortage of funds for replenishment. (30th Dispatch)

Military Attaches from Various Countries 9

Negotiating Boundary Demarcation in Jinzhou

Awaiting Instructions from the United States

(Beiping) A dispatch from Jinzhou states that military attachés from various countries who came to Jinzhou for inspection, including those from Britain, France, and Germany, have received instructions from their respective governments to discuss the issue of demarcating neutral zones. They are awaiting instructions from the United States before they can proceed with consultations. According to the opinion of one military attaché, the demarcation of zones must use rivers and mountains as the standard. British Counselor Stuart Bodman went to Panshan for inspection on the afternoon of the 29th and is scheduled to return to Jinzhou on the 30th. US Counselor Ord went to the Daling River for inspection. (30th Dispatch)

Jinzhou Situation Eases 10

Japanese Troops on Beining Line Withdraw in Three Sections

Passenger Train Only Reached Dahushan Yesterday

(Beiping) A dispatch from Jinzhou states that the situation east of Jinzhou has eased. The Japanese army removed the obstacles from the Raoyang River railway bridge. The armored vehicles of the Japanese army at Lijia Wopu and the infantry, cavalry, and artillery around the Raoyang River withdrew eastward in three sections. The first section withdrew from Raoyang River to Baiqibao at 11 PM on the 28th. The second section withdrew from Lijia Wopu to Raoyang River at 8 AM on the 29th. In the last section, there are no Japanese troops from Lijia Wopu to Xinmin. Japanese planes flew low over Jinzhou and the Daling River at noon on the 29th for reconnaissance. Our armored vehicles are still stationed at Lijia Wopu. All telephone and telegraph lines along the way that were damaged by the Japanese army are now being repaired urgently, as evidence of Japanese provocation against us. However, the sections of the Beining Railway that were bombed by the Japanese army have not yet been repaired. (30th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Japanese army is withdrawing from Xinmin and Juliuhe. There is still a small part of the Japanese army west of Dahushan. The passenger train traveling east on the Beining Line on the 30th only reached Dahushan. Residents of various stations have been flocking to Shanhaiguan to escape, and about 140 people have come to Beiping for refuge today. (30th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Japanese soldiers are reinforcing Yingkou again. On the 29th, they conducted a large artillery exercise in the area. There are no Japanese soldiers in Panshan and Dawa. A Japanese plane flew to Dahushan at 11 AM for reconnaissance. (30th Dispatch)

(Shenyang) Japanese troops are successively withdrawing to the east bank of the Liao River and will soon be completely withdrawn, while Chinese troops are gradually advancing to occupy the land vacated by the Japanese troops. This is being carried out according to procedure. However, the Japanese claim that the Chinese troops are gathering in excessive numbers. An article was recently published by Japanese officials stating that aircraft inspections revealed that between 2:00 PM and 4:00 PM yesterday, there were seven trains seemingly fully loaded with Chinese troops traveling from Jinzhou to Dahushan, and there were still 1,300 infantrymen, 1,000 cavalrymen, and over 50 artillery pieces stationed near Dahushan. When reporters inquired about the Japanese army headquarters' opinion on this, a spokesperson said that if there were no provocative acts, the Japanese army did not want to attack the Chinese troops there. When reporters inquired whether the current movements of the Chinese troops would be considered provocative by the Japanese army, the spokesperson replied that it had not yet been determined. Foreign staff members of the Beining Railway declared that the Beining Railway could resume traffic tomorrow. Judging from this, the road is now peaceful, which can be imagined. The Japanese army headquarters has now allowed a train to be test-run today to inspect the route and repair telephone and telegraph communications. (30th Reuters Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Jinzhou telegram: The "Zhongshan" armored vehicle carried road bureau technicians from Dahushan at 1:00 AM on the 30th to repair the power lines east of Tangjiawopu and returned to Dahushan at 5:00 AM to report that there were no Japanese troops from Xinmin to Tangjiawopu. The Japanese troops at Juliuhe have not withdrawn. The rumor that Xiaobailong occupied Xinmin is not accurate, but he is actively recruiting followers. Due to a shortage of firearms, most are organized as broadsword teams. At 8:30 AM, another train departed from Dahushan to Xinmin to continue repairing the power lines. Counselors from various embassies went to Beipiao at 9:00 AM to inspect. (30th Dispatch)

Bombing Incident at Japanese Military Attache's Residence in Beiping 11

Bao Yulin Visits Yano Shin

Expresses Determination to Investigate the Case

(Beiping) A bomb exploded at the residence of Japanese naval attache Lieutenant Commander Sakai in Dingxiang Hutong last night. After the explosion, the Public Security Bureau, in conjunction with the Japanese authorities, is conducting a rigorous investigation. Bao Yulin, the Director of the Public Security Bureau, visited Yano Shin, the acting representative of the Japanese embassy today, expressing his determination to be responsible for investigating the case. Yano stated that he would consult with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs before further contact. (30th Dispatch)

(Beiping) The house where the naval counselor of the Japanese embassy lives, which is located outside the embassy street, suddenly had a burst of explosives last night. It is thought to be a bomb explosion. No deaths or injuries have been reported. The Japanese naval counselor is currently in Tianjin. (30th Reuters Dispatch)

Zhang Xueliang 12

Issued a Statement Last Night

No Agreement with Yano

(Beiping) Zhang Xueliang issued a statement tonight stating that Yano's visit the night before last has been greatly misinterpreted by outsiders. Yano did informally solicit his opinion on the issue of neutral zones, but rumors about any kind of agreement, signing, or understanding are inaccurate. (30th Dispatch)

Rumors of Bandits Occupying Yingkou 13

(Beiping) Five or six hundred bandits from Niuzhuang used heavy artillery to cover their crossing of the Liao River at noon on the 29th and occupied Yingkou. (30th Dispatch)

Zhu Guangmu and Others Go to Jinzhou 14

(Beiping) Zhu Guangmu and Cai Yuanfeng, under Zhang Xueliang's orders, are going to Jinzhou tonight to inspect the various situations and to negotiate diplomatic issues. (30th Dispatch)

Japanese Ambassador Visits Gu Weijun 15

Discusses the Jinzhou Incident

No Concrete Decisions

(Nanjing) Shigemitsu Aoi, the Japanese ambassador to China, arrived in Beijing at 7:00 AM on the 30th. He first agreed on a meeting time with Foreign Minister Gu Weijun on the 29th through the Japanese consul in Beijing, Uemura. Shigemitsu went to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 4:00 PM on the 30th, where Gu met him in his office. Shigemitsu first extended his congratulations, and then exchanged views on the establishment of a neutral zone in Jinzhou and the aftermath of the Tianjin incident. He expressed his willingness to discuss with Representative Shi and the northern authorities via telegram, so no concrete decisions were made at that time. Shigemitsu left at 6:00 PM. (3rd Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Japanese Ambassador to China, Shigemitsu Aoi, went from Shanghai to Nanjing last night to discuss the issue of the Manchurian neutral zone with Foreign Minister Gu. It is hoped here that this discussion can open the way for direct Sino-Japanese negotiations on the entire Manchurian issue. Political circles in Tokyo remain optimistic about the future of the overall situation, believing that great progress can be made soon. The situation in Tianjin is still considered serious, but the authorities concerned seem to believe that Zhang Xueliang will be able to restrain his troops and quickly restore local security and order. (30th Reuters Dispatch)

Acting Minister of Foreign Affairs 16

Gu Weijun Assumes Office Yesterday

Lin Sen Represents the Central Government to Administer the Oath

Chairman Chiang Has a Personally Written Admonition

(Nanjing) The newly appointed Acting Minister of Foreign Affairs, Gu Weijun, held an oath-taking ceremony at the National Government Auditorium at 10:30 AM on the 30th. Lin Sen was appointed by the Central Government to administer the oath. After the ceremony, Chairman Chiang presented the seal, Gu received the seal, then Gu raised his right hand and read the oath. Lin Sen administered the oath. After the oath, Lin gave a speech, stating that at this time of national crisis and diplomatic urgency, the Central Government paid very close attention to the selection of diplomatic personnel. Everyone knew that Shaochuan (Gu Weijun) had a wealth of diplomatic talent and experience, so this great responsibility

Page 8

was entrusted to him. This was not only considered satisfactory, but the Central Committee members were also very pleased. With regard to diplomatic tasks, we should, in principle, deal with foreign countries in a revolutionary spirit based on the teachings of the Premier, but internally, we should pay attention to the reorganization and training of the ministry's affairs. Recently, I had the opportunity to travel and visit overseas, where China has sent embassies and consulates, and I also carefully examined the service of the staff of the embassies and consulates. I noticed one thing that was quite inappropriate, namely that many of the staff of the embassies and consulates were young people under the age of thirty. It is of course gratifying to see young people with potential, and although there are young people in the diplomatic circles of foreign countries, it is not as widespread as this. Although many young people have vigor, some take the opportunity to study abroad, which is good, but it is not as good as completing training in China before being dispatched abroad to serve wholeheartedly, so that both knowledge and experience are sufficient. After working hours, if there is any remaining strength, further research can be conducted concurrently, which is not mutually exclusive. This is what is hoped for those who are reorganizing the ministry. Secondly, during this inspection of various places, overseas Chinese strongly hope that those who send embassy and consulate personnel must be familiar with the Party's doctrines, so that they can effectively cooperate with the local Party branches at all levels. Now, when the country is in distress and there are many difficulties in diplomatic affairs, but if we can act in accordance with the Premier's instructions, we will surely achieve the final victory. When the Premier was dying in Beijing, he said, "Peaceful struggle to save China," and if we use these words to negotiate with various countries, then the final victory will naturally be achieved. Finally, I wish Shaochuan good health and progress. Then Chiang's speech was delivered, followed by Gu's reply, and the event was adjourned. (30th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Acting Foreign Minister Gu Weijun took office on the morning of the 30th after the National Government's memorial week. Chairman Chiang personally wrote a speech, the original text of which is as follows:

War is not limited to tangible military affairs. The wars of agriculture, industry, commerce, science, and economics are more effective than military force, and the value of the intangible wars in diplomacy is greater than that of any other war, but the world does not know this. In military warfare, there are those who defend by attacking, those who retreat by advancing, and those who defend by attacking and retreat by advancing. The wonder of its ingenious and realistic use depends on the one mind of the commander-in-chief. The efforts of diplomatic negotiations, the distance of its efforts, and the magnitude of its effects are far greater than those of military affairs by a hundred or a thousand times. This also depends on the specialization of the appointment and the doubling of the trust, so that the diplomatic authorities can be responsible for courageously advancing in order to save the final victory. It is a pity that the world only sees tangible warfare as warfare, and does not know that intangible warfare is more than tangible warfare. They only see the current war as war, and do not know that today's war was already started invisibly decades ago, but it was only discovered today, and the number of its victories and defeats had already been determined. In these decades of intangible warfare, it has not started from today. However, although the number of past victories and defeats has already been determined, the victories and defeats of future wars can be determined today. As the saying goes, "If you lose in the east, you can make it up in the west. It is not too late to mend the fold after losing the sheep." Now Minister Gu is taking office in the autumn of crisis and is ordered at the intersection of survival and death. I am deeply convinced that he will surely shoulder the arduous task and not disgrace his mission. However, military affairs lie in the specialization of trust, so outside the tent, the general is in charge. Diplomatic relations are more important than military affairs, especially in the specialization of trust. To resist foreign aggression, we must first settle the internal affairs. Only unification can resist insult. There has never been a country that has not been unified and can win abroad. Therefore, today's foreign affairs, whether resolved by military means or by diplomatic means, will not be successful without first seeking domestic unity. To advocate war, we must first seek domestic unity. Even to advocate peace, we must also seek domestic unity, otherwise we cannot talk about peace. Therefore, if we cannot fight, we cannot talk about peace, and if we are not unified, we cannot talk about peace or war.

When our country is facing internal and external troubles, the authorities in military and diplomatic affairs can only rely on a sincere patriotic zeal, exhaust their loyalty and fulfill their responsibilities. As for success or failure, profit or loss, they cannot foresee it. Praise or blame, honor or disgrace, are not what they care about. The government and the people must have specialized trust, unite together, and serve as the country's backing, without seeking quick success in the moment, but planning for effectiveness in the future. The Premier said, "If we control it, we will survive; if others control it, we will perish." This is the Premier's unchanging legacy of diplomatic policy. The diplomatic policy of the Special Diplomatic Committee is the only appropriate policy for today. Minister Gu should deeply understand this meaning, be mindful of the legacy, display his ambitions, and give full play to his talents, so that our country's diplomacy can turn defeat into victory and turn danger into safety, so as not to fail the government and the people's eager expectations. Chiang Kai-shek, November 30, 20th year. (30th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Gu Weijun, accompanied by Political Vice Minister Li Jinlun, went to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 11:00 AM on the 30th to attend the ministry's memorial week. After giving a speech to all the staff, he issued a ministerial order appointing Jin Wensi as the Director of the General Affairs Department and temporarily acting as the Permanent Vice Minister, Yang Yongqing as the Secretary of the Simplified Appointment, and Huang Yuding as the Assistant of the General Affairs Department and concurrently the Chief of the Accounting and Disbursement Section. It is also rumored that there will be changes to the Director of the Intelligence Department, Diao Minqian. (30th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The newly appointed Acting Minister of Foreign Affairs, Gu Weijun, went to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 11:00 AM on the 30th after taking office at the National Government in the morning and summoned the staff for a speech in the Ministry's auditorium. First, Vice Minister Li Jinlun delivered a welcoming speech on behalf of all the staff. After the speech, Gu gave a speech, stating that he had not been involved in politics for two years. Now, due to the current national crisis, he had repeatedly received telegrams from the Central Party and government authorities and Chairman Chiang, summoning him to Beijing to participate in the Special Diplomatic Committee. Later, he was ordered to act as the Minister of Foreign Affairs and had repeatedly declined, but his request was not approved. Soon after, the appointment was changed to a clearly signed order for him to take office immediately. In the future, he hoped that everyone would assist him with the same spirit that they had assisted Minister Wang and Minister Li over the past few years. If there were any opinions, they could be raised at any time for research. He would take full responsibility for matters and had no problems with people. However, he hoped that Minister Shi would complete the affairs of the League of Nations as soon as possible and come to Beijing to take office, so that he could be relieved of his responsibilities as soon as possible. (30th Dispatch)

Announced Abolition Yesterday

(Nanjing) The Headquarters of the Army, Navy, and Air Force was officially abolished on the 30th. The original staff office was transferred to the General Staff Headquarters and the Directorate General of Training. The business office was transferred to the Storage Department and the Ordnance Department of the Military Supplies Department. The transportation office was transferred to the Transportation Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs. The adjutant office was transferred to the newly organized Chairman's Residence Office and the Directorate General of Military Medicine of the Ministry of Military Affairs. All councilors, counselors, consultants, and other personnel, if they are civil servants, will be sent to the Civil Service Department of the National Government for appointment. If they are military officers, they will be assigned to the Military Counselor's Office of the National Government and the Military Advisory Council for appointment. As for the staff of the business office and staff office, except for 20% who will remain to handle the closing, the rest will be assigned to the Ministry of Military Affairs and the General Staff Headquarters and other agencies for appointment. If there is no suitable vacancy, they will temporarily be on standby. If they voluntarily resign, they will be given one month's gratuity. All are required to be completed by December 8. (30th Dispatch)

Ministry of Industry Plans to Refine Cod Liver Oil 34

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industry, recognizing cod liver oil as a nourishing tonic with a wide market, noted that the raw materials are produced in our country but are refined by foreign merchants and then sold back to our country, resulting in significant financial losses. It has now ordered the Qingdao Commodity Inspection Bureau to send personnel to Shidao and other places to hire workers to collect these raw materials, first to fry them into crude oil, and then send them to the Industrial Testing Ground of the Ministry of Industry for chemical analysis, and use scientific methods to refine them. According to the Ministry of Industry's fish technology expert, self-producing domestic cod liver oil can reduce the outflow of hundreds of thousands of yuan each year. (30th Special Dispatch)

Florentin Returns from England 46

Guomin, 30th Paris Telegram: French Finance Minister Florentin returned to Paris today after visiting England at the end of the week. Major Drug Manufacturing Case Finalized 47

Reuters, 30th Basel Telegram: The major drug manufacturing case was finalized today. The main offender, Muller, was sentenced to one month in prison and fined 20,000 Swiss francs. Among the other convicts was the Italian Barenari, who was sentenced to six months in prison and fined 10,000 Swiss francs, and Geneva chemist Rochu, who was sentenced to four months in prison and fined 10,000 Swiss francs. Muller's wife was acquitted but had to pay part of the court costs, requiring 20,000 Swiss francs. This case involved countries in Central Europe and the East, and almost all major cities in the world were indirectly related. The League of Nations sent representatives to observe the trial. During the trial, there were shocking discoveries that the group had used cans for infant milk powder to smuggle heroin to Germany. The discovery of this case dates back to November 15, 1929, when customs officials in Alexandria, Egypt, seized 20 boxes of heroin disguised as tallow on the Italian ship Esperia. After a long period of investigation, it was finally found that its manufacturing facility was in Basel, and distribution facilities were set up all over the world. Muller was the main manufacturer, and the drugs he manufactured were worth more than 600,000 pounds in British currency.

Important News

Japanese Army 51

Tianjin Under Cannon Attack

Japanese Army Fires Cannon Shells Used by Bandits

Japanese Marines and Firearms Arrive in Tianjin Successively

Tianjin Correspondence: Since the night of the 26th, under the cover of the Japanese army, plainclothes teams re-enacted the second riot in places like Ningjia Bridge and Wandezhuang. The Japanese have now torn off their mask of hypocrisy and openly and fiercely bombard the Chinese-controlled areas with constant artillery fire, desperately seeking provocations and hoping to create a direct conflict between China and Japan in order to realize a chaotic situation. The dispatch of the plainclothes teams was mixed with and guided by the Japanese, and their momentum was fiercer than last time, and the artillery fire was also denser than last time. Fortunately, our side's defenses were very strict, and the bandits were still unable to break through. The original plan of the Japanese side was to use deceptive means to make our side withdraw all defensive works, and then use a blitzkrieg method to seize Tianjin and cut off the Beining Railway line, so that Jinzhou and other places could be settled without bloodshed. Now that this kind of cunning plan has failed, it has taken a sharp turn for the worse. As early as 10:00 am yesterday (the 27th), unreasonable demands were made, using this as an excuse to take hostile actions. In addition to refuting the claims based on reason, the authorities have also made various preparations. The following records the situation yesterday:

Japanese Army Bombards Day and Night After the second riot on the night of the 26th, the Japanese military camp at Haiguang Temple and various places in the Japanese Concession continued to fire guns and cannons at us. The sounds temporarily stopped after 3:00 am yesterday (the 27th), but by 7:00 am, the tension suddenly reappeared, and the sound of artillery was loud. The artillery shells were all fired from the Japanese military camp at Haiguang Temple, covering the plainclothes teams in Ningjia Bridge, Huaiqingli, and Paotaizhuang Xiaotili, attacking our defensive sections. The momentum was fierce, but after a head-on attack by the security team, many were killed on the spot, and several were captured. The rioters retreated to their starting point, and then the situation calmed down, but the sound of gunfire was still intermittent. Until 2:00 pm, the Japanese military camp fired more than 40 artillery shells, falling within our territory. Among them, there were ten 10-cm semi-diameter, 40-cm long cannon shells, and 7-cm semi-diameter mountain cannons and field cannons. Although some of them exploded, they did not hit any vital points. At the same time, the Japanese army also appeared on Rongye Street, carrying machine guns to nearby locations of our defense area and advancing towards the southeast corner of the city, intending to challenge. Because our security team maintained calmness and ignored them, they hesitated and retreated, still firing guns and shooting at our side from time to time. Plainclothes teams lurking in Xiaotili and Huaiqingli launched two sudden attacks on our side, but were bravely repelled by the security team. The bandits suffered many casualties. Five of our police officers, Li Lianfu, Zhang Qinxue, Sun Xiuyan, Wang Zizhou, and Wu Zhumi, were injured, and about seven or eight were killed in action. Section Chief Tian, who was originally stationed in the Sixth Section of the First District, personally led the police officers to fight against the plainclothes teams, and was never broken into. Now, because the situation in that section is dangerously pressing, it has been moved to the Qinyunlou Security 17th Team's stationed location in the South City at 6:00 am this morning, as a temporary office location. During the fierce battle the previous night, at about 10:00 pm, the Japanese army secretly transported more than 50 plainclothes teams by small boats along the riverbank of the Zhaikou, hoping to attack the Second Special District. After being discovered by the police officers, they opened fire to intercept them. The bandits lost their footing and fell into the water one after another, and many drowned. There were still plainclothes teams appearing in Zhaikou and Paotai, and fierce battles continued to occur. All were bravely repelled by the police officers, and were unable to break through the defense line. The Fifth Company of the Second Brigade and the Twentieth Company of the Third Brigade of the Security Team were all injured, but the number of people was not large. Until about 2:00 am this morning (the 28th), plainclothes teams gathered again on Zhaikou Road, Rongye Street Road, and Haiguang Temple Road, one way towards Ningjia Bridge, and one way towards Nanguan Street, and launched a large-scale attack on our defense line at the same time. The Japanese side fired artillery to cover them, intending to use the power of the artillery fire and the momentum of the concerted action to make our side unable to take care of both ends, and break through one or two defense lines. So for a time, the sound of guns and cannons was loud, and the momentum was quite fierce. However, the security team resisted bravely, and the plainclothes teams from all directions were unsuccessful and were all repelled. After about half an hour of fierce fighting, it entered a state of standstill. After 3:00 am, the sound of guns and cannons became sparse again, but there were still faint sounds, and there were no other changes.

Unreasonable Demands from the Japanese Side Commander Kashi Haohei of the Japanese Army stationed in Tianjin presented five demands to Wang Shuchang, Chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government, at 10:30 am yesterday (the 27th), asking for a reply by noon on the same day. The translated text reads, "To His Excellency Wang Shuchang, Chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government and Commander of the Second Army: On November 15th, Your Excellency expressed your apologies for the hostile actions of the Chinese side. However, yesterday, the 26th, your country's army and security team suddenly fired at the Japanese army and the Japanese Concession, and this has not been stopped until the 27th. This clearly shows that you have no sincerity in acknowledging hostile actions against the Japanese army. Now, in order to maintain peace between China and Japan, the Commander of the Japanese Army hereby demands the following items from Your Excellency, to be implemented by noon on the 27th, and hopes for a reply: (1) Immediately cease hostile acts; (2) The Chinese army must withdraw 20 li from the garrisons of all countries; (3) The armed security team must withdraw from the Nanyun River and Jingang Bridge, passing through the Qiangzi River, to the north of the Yun River; (4) The army in Hebei Province (whether armed or in plainclothes) must cease moving; (5) Absolutely prohibit anti-Japanese and insulting Japanese behavior."

Our Side's Stern Refutation After receiving the above demands from the Japanese side, Chairman Wang of the Provincial Government immediately notified the Japanese military commander that it was still necessary to translate, so he verbally agreed to reply before 6:00 pm yesterday (the 27th). At 4:00 pm, he sent a letter to Kashi, stating that the Commander's note of the 27th of this month had been translated and understood, and now replied in accordance with the original items, etc. The general idea of ​​the reply is as follows: (1) Currently, our side is defending against plainclothes teams, and there is absolutely no hostile behavior towards your side. After repeated statements, I hope you can understand. Our two sides have always maintained good relations, and I especially hope that we can work together to prevent similar hostile actions in the future; (2) In order to respect the intention of the exchange of notes on the Tianjin Treaty of 1902, our side has withdrawn a small number of Chinese troops temporarily stationed in Tianjin to a location 20 li outside Tianjin, and has already replied to your country's consul general on file; (3) The Tianjin Municipal Security Team has the responsibility to protect the public security of Tianjin. Now that there are plainclothes teams causing trouble, if the security team is withdrawn in accordance with the letter, the lives and property of Chinese and foreign people in the withdrawn area will inevitably be impossible to protect. It is really difficult to withdraw suddenly. I hope your side can understand this fact, but if we can jointly find effective methods to protect public security with the authorities of other friendly countries stationed in Tianjin, this article can also be discussed and handled; (4) The Chinese troops currently stationed within 20 li of Tianjin have already been withdrawn as mentioned above. As for other troops, there is no movement towards Tianjin; (5) Anti-Japanese and insulting behavior has been prohibited for a long time, and we should pay more attention to it in the future.

Damage Situation on Our Side Yesterday afternoon (the 27th), the consuls of the United States and Belgium stationed in Tianjin, accompanied by a military attache from the American military camp, went to Dongfu Bridge, Dongmalu Southeast Corner, Nanguan Xiatou, etc., accompanied by Zhang Guanru, Secretary of the Municipal Government, to conduct on-the-spot investigations. Upon returning, they stated that there were two types of artillery shells found in the Chinese territory, one was a 12-cm over-mountain cannon, and the other was a 75-cm shrapnel. There was also the most powerful bomb, as big as a dustpan. The American military officer said that this bomb explodes in mid-air, and when it lands, it can explode a very large area. American robbers often use it. It is inhumane to fire such artillery shells, so it is prohibited for use in foreign countries, especially in urban areas. A total of more than 30 artillery shells were fired on the night of the 26th, and more than 10 fell around the Provincial Government and in the river. The large glass window of the front building of the Provincial Government was shattered by the explosion. One shell fell on the Huangweilu Municipal Slaughterhouse, exploding on a tree, scraping the corner of the wall, and there was not much damage. One shell fell in front of the Public Security Bureau. The most tragic thing was that a 12-cm over-mountain cannon shell fell on Dongmalu, killing two policemen and injuring five others. When they arrived at Nanguan Xiatou, the plainclothes teams were still firing at the security team from the roof of the Methodist Church. The south end of the main street in that area was the Japanese defense line, and the north end was the security team's defense line. On the evening of the 26th, dozens of plainclothes teams suddenly rushed out from within the Japanese defense line and advanced to only a dozen paces away from the security team. The security team immediately opened machine gun fire to sweep them, and the plainclothes teams retreated one after another. At that time, the Japanese army within the Japanese defense line suddenly fired at the security team. The first shot was too close, the second shot was too far, and the third shot landed on the security team's defense line, blasting a circular hole in the sandbag. One security team member was killed on the spot, and two were injured. The situation was extremely tragic. About five or six artillery shells landed near the defense line of the Fifth Company of the Second Brigade of the Zhaikou Security Team. Although there were no inscriptions on the artillery shells, the shell casings all had the words "Taisho 15th Year" on them, proving that they were issued to the plainclothes teams by the Japanese. In this battle, five policemen were killed and more than ten were injured, all of which were eyewitnessed facts.

Emergency Meeting of the Diplomatic Corps After the consuls and military attachés were guided by personnel from the Municipal Government to inspect yesterday (the 27th), they all believed that the Japanese army's shelling of the Chinese-controlled areas was destructive and inhumane. It has been decided to hold an emergency meeting at 9:00 am today (the 28th) to discuss ways to provide relief to the city and maintain public security, and they greatly disapprove of the five demands made by Japanese Commander Kashi. The current situation is clearly that the Japanese side is making unreasonable demands, and the issue of demanding that China withdraw the security team is not something that the Japanese side should raise.

Japanese Marines Arrive in Tianjin The two Japanese ships, "Fuyong" and "Asagao", which were docked in Tanggu, were divided into batches, carrying about 200 marines. One batch of 90 men, carrying two machine guns and four portable ones, as well as several boxes of ammunition, set off for Tianjin yesterday (the 27th), passing through Gegu at 6:00 pm. After another batch arrived in Tianjin, they landed at Dalian Wharf. The Japanese Command dispatched eight heavy-duty vehicles to transport about a hundred Japanese soldiers to Haiguang Temple. When the Japanese soldiers landed, the wharf was under martial law, and four machine guns were installed to cover the landing. According to foreign news, the Japanese army's "Henan Maru", which was sailing from Dalian to Tianjin, was loaded with 500 pistols, 20 small steel cannons, 30 machine guns, and 200 boxes of gun ammunition, specifically for the purpose of using rioters to disrupt the rear. Also, Japanese Commander Kashi telegraphed Shenyang to request four aircraft to be flown from the air to Tianjin to prepare for disrupting the area.

Wartime State in the Japanese Concession After the incident broke out again on the evening of the 26th, the Japanese Concession's defenses became stricter again. Earlier, most of the defensive works in the Concession had not been removed, so they were strictly repaired again. The various barriers were raised separately and covered with steel plates. Sandbags were piled up around the roofs and spires of companies such as Zhongyuan Company and Lao Jiuzhang, and gun positions and machine guns were set up. Defensive works were also built on the east and northwest corners of the roof of Mitsui & Co., a Japanese merchant in the riverbank, and five small steel cannons with a diameter of 42 cm were set up, facing directly at the Public Security Bureau, Ningjia Bridge, and Haiguang Temple and other places. The Japanese army also chose a high place to set up cannons, intending to inflict heavy blows on our policemen, merchants, and civilians with the power of the artillery fire. Japanese Army Commander Kashi Haohei also issued a declaration yesterday and announced martial law at the same time, posting a notice saying, "According to the martial law, the Tianjin Japanese Concession is designated as an enclosed area," clearly indicating a wartime state, and declaring that those who do not obey will be killed without mercy. As a result, the people in the Concession were extremely shaken, and Chinese and Japanese merchants and civilians moved to the British and French Concessions one after another. At 8:00 am, the Japanese soldiers once prevented passage, but because the Japanese were also moving, all were allowed to move out. Now, the Concession has become a scene where ten out of ten houses are empty. However, people outside the Concession are not allowed to enter the Concession, even those holding passes are not allowed to pass. According to reports, Japanese expatriates recently received an urgent order from the Japanese Consul General in Tianjin, allowing them to freely move to safe areas. Those who do not want to leave the Concession are gathered separately in the Jiangnan Foreign Firm or public hospitals, etc.

Japanese expatriates have moved to the British and French Concessions for temporary residence, and some have already returned to their country. However, most of those who have moved out this time are Japanese and Korean women and children, and the adult men are still waiting for orders in the Concession area. The volunteer army was fully armed and dispatched yesterday, totaling 462 people, stationed at various street intersections. The number of people is also planned to be increased due to the cause of today and tomorrow (November 28).

Japanese Army Withdraws Separately 52

The Effect of the Withdrawal is Unclear

Liaoning and Jilin are Not Abandoned

The Great Beauty Evening News, Shenyang, 28th: The reason for the Japanese army's sudden withdrawal is still unknown here, but Kwantung Commander Honjo seems to have decided to immediately begin withdrawing from the South Manchuria Railway (SMR) zone. According to a spokesperson for the Japanese command today, the Japanese army on the Beining Railway will begin to withdraw tonight. The Japanese command has notified the expatriates in the Japanese Concession to prepare to lodge military officers in their homes starting tonight. When reporters asked about the extent of the withdrawal, he replied that they would first restore the situation before the occupation of Qiqihar. This means that except for Zhengjiatun, Jilin City, Juliao River, and Yingkou, where the Japanese army is still stationed, all the remaining Japanese troops will be withdrawn to the SMR zone. It is said that the final batch of soldiers will not be completely withdrawn to the SMR zone, restoring the situation before September 18th, until the final adjustment of the political situation between China and Japan. It is also heard that the Japanese army coming from Korea will be sent back to their original defenses immediately because the situation in Korea is critical. American missionaries who came to Shenyang from Korea all said that the Koreans in various places are thinking of taking the opportunity to launch an independent uprising, which is imminent.

Continued Telegram at Noon: A spokesperson for the Japanese command suddenly and unofficially issued a news release to various newspapers, titled "Kwantung Army's Attitude Towards Jinzhou," which stated that the Shenyang Japanese army, in view of the emergency situation in Tianjin, decided to take necessary steps to allocate defensive forces. Now that the situation in Tianjin has improved, it has been decided to withdraw all the troops sent to Jinzhou back to east of the Liao River and the SMR zone to await future developments in the situation. The Japanese army has now begun to withdraw, and the troops stationed outside the SMR zone will be gradually reduced to the minimum limit. West of the Liao River, except for a few Japanese troops left to protect the Japanese consulate in Xinmin, the Japanese troops in other places are withdrawing. It was also officially announced that Captain Itakura led a reconnaissance squad on an armored train to the east of the Rao River, where they encountered the Chinese army. Itakura and a railway worker were shot and killed, and two South Manchuria Railway workers were injured. Finally, a spokesperson for the Japanese command denied that the sudden withdrawal of troops was due to political developments in Geneva and Tokyo, claiming that it was only a strategy.

Continued Telegram in the Evening: The Japanese army on the Beining Railway has begun to withdraw. At about 6:00 pm today, two trains loaded with soldiers, artillery, and other military supplies returned to the SMR zone. Diplomatic circles, military attachés of the League of Nations inspection representatives, and foreign newspaper correspondents have commented on this matter. Some foreign newspaper correspondents and military inspectors decided to celebrate, believing that it was the result of the second Kailuo format war in the three northeastern provinces. There are various rumors about the reasons for the withdrawal of troops. Some said it was due to pressure from New York bankers, some said it was due to the British opposition to the Japanese army's occupation of the Beining Railway, some said it was because the League of Nations would send an investigation team, and others said it was due to political reasons in Tokyo. There are also rumors that Doihara has signed a secret peace agreement with the Chinese military authorities in Tianjin. Foreign military inspectors who came to Shenyang from Tokyo still set off for Jinzhou this morning in a special car prepared by Bonkyo, and they must have been surprised when they saw the Japanese troop cars returning in droves on the way. It was also heard that a team of Chinese stragglers, seemingly informed of the Japanese withdrawal, dug up the railway several miles outside Xinmin, causing the Japanese army's withdrawal to be delayed for some time, and it was only after the engineering car was sent to repair it that it could pass. The reporter recently went to Huanggu Tun Station and heard that from 5:00 am to midnight yesterday, the station had passed 13 Japanese troop trains, a total of 221 cars. At 7:10 am this morning, a supply car was also passed, all heading towards Jinzhou. However, when the reporter arrived at the station, it was as quiet as death. The British engineer has returned to Shenyang, and only a Chinese staff member remains at the station to take care of it. As for the Qiqihar and Taoang Railway lines, according to a spokesperson for the Japanese command, a large detachment of the Qiqihar garrison will be withdrawn soon, and the Japanese army in Taonan may also be withdrawn.

Japanese Army Digs Up 53

Beining Railway Police's Hidden Weapons

Railway Staff Detained and Tortured in Various Ways Such as in the Toilet

Beiping Correspondence: Since the September 18th Incident, the Beining Railway secretly buried the firearms used by the railway police in the public residence of the railway staff at the north entrance of Sanjing Road in the Shenyang Commercial Port. Unexpectedly, it was detected by the Japanese army, and dozens of Japanese soldiers with iron helmets suddenly went to search and dig up the area on the 11th of this month. Almost all the firearms were searched and taken away (at that time, the railway staff in the residence were interrogated with various means, forced and threatened, and detained in the toilet, forced to eat urine residue, and tortured in every possible way. According to the people who came from Shenyang, the Japanese army's tyrannical situation at that time is really infuriating.

Since the incident, the Beining Railway Office in Shenyang has been unable to perform its duties, so it has been moved to Jinzhou. However, more than a dozen deputy section chiefs, Zhang Baohua, and staff members were still sent to stay in Shenyang. On the 11th of this month, when the deputy section chief and others gathered at the railway's public residence on Sanjing Road in the commercial port, more than 20 Japanese soldiers with iron helmets suddenly broke into the courtyard with guns at 0:30 pm. They immediately asked where the toilet was and forcibly led the clerk Wang Weilun to the toilet. After digging in various places for a long time, they found nothing. Then they smashed the doors of each room and searched through the houses, but found nothing. Then they entered the board room in the northwest corner of the backyard, pushed down the board wall, and dug in the ground. They found all the rifles, portable machine guns, mortars, pistols, and ammunition buried there by order of the Fengtian Provincial Government. They then forced all the more than a dozen staff members in the residence, including Zhang Baohua and Zhang Fengxian, as well as a child of a staff member, to gather in the center of the courtyard and interrogated them by name about who hid the firearms and where Director Hu was now. If they lied, they would be shot to death. The staff members all replied that the Beining Railway Office in Shenyang had long ceased to function, and the rest of them were staying here temporarily because they had no money to go home. As for the burying of firearms, it may have been done by the railway police when they fled in a hurry. They really did not know the details and did not know where Director Hu was.

The Japanese soldiers had no choice but to order Wang Weilun to lead them to the living room, smash open the rooms of the public residence administrator Liu Shiyuan and the office desk, and take away a string of keys to the various gates of the main station, the key to the treasury of the General Affairs Section, and Liu Shiyuan's photo. They returned to the courtyard, searched the pockets of each person's clothes, and drove them all into the South Warehouse, forcing them into one room and guarding them with soldiers. They also forced several servants to go to the backyard to help load the searched firearms into heavy-duty vehicles and transport them away one after another. At the same time, they also loaded more than a dozen people, including Zhang Baohua, into a car and drove them to the Japanese army headquarters at the South Manchuria Hospital at the Japanese station. They drove them into the underground toilet of the department where prisoners were detained. The floor was full of feces and urine, there were no doors and windows, the stench was foul, and it was extremely cold. They were forced to sit around in one corner and were not allowed to speak or move. Guards were stationed all around. The guards repeatedly beat and insulted them, ordered them to eat the feces and urine that had been left behind, threatened them with their hands raising guns and bayonets, and inflicted various tortures such as hitting their heads with sticks and pulling out their hair. At more than 10:00 am the next morning, Zhang Baohua was brought in for interrogation, and then Zhang Fengxian and others were taken away separately to inquire about the hidden firearms. The answers were the same as before. Until 2:00 pm, the Japanese army saw that they could not get any information, so they released Zhang Baohua and others first. Finally, they brought in Zhang Boren, a clerk, and more than a dozen servants and interrogated them about the hiding of firearms. They also kicked and beat the servants vigorously, but they did not confess any other information. Earlier, several employees escaped from the guardhouse when the Japanese soldiers broke in, and hastily reported the above situation to the General Bureau. Upon receiving the report, the General Bureau urgently telegraphed Stiehl, the director of the transportation office stationed in Shenyang, to go and negotiate. When Stiehl rushed to the Japanese army headquarters, more than a dozen employees had been completely released at about the evening of that day. The Railway Bureau felt deeply sorry for the fact that the employees had been detained for a day and night, frozen, starved, and frightened, and had been abused. It has sent personnel to express condolences and provided consolation money to show its consideration. It is said that this incident was caused by a former clerk of the bureau who had been dismissed for wrongdoing, who harbored a grudge and reported it to the Japanese army. If so, then that clerk is helping the tiger to harm others, and his flesh is still edible (November 27).

Regarding the Shenyang Incident 54

Japanese Centered Public Opinion

Implying the Maturity of the Second Phase of Continental Policy

Tokyo Correspondence: From the Shenyang Incident on September 18th until recently, two months have passed. The former bustling customs post is now desolate and filled with sorrow, and the problem remains shrouded in dark clouds. Now, temporarily avoiding a review of the facts, let us introduce some Japanese public opinions regarding the Shenyang Incident. Isn't the intention of the Japanese people already obvious?

Firstly, this is the proposition of a powerful Japanese opposition party (Seiyukai). It has four concrete central ideas: (1) Manchuria and Mongolia, in terms of their position in the Far East and historical relationship, are entirely special regions unrelated to China. (2) The entire region of Manchuria and Mongolia should promote economic development based on the principles of "Open Door" and "Equal Opportunity," while also making Manchuria and Mongolia a place of residence for both internal and external people. (3) Maintain the security of Manchuria and Mongolia and steadfastly protect Japan's rights and interests. (4) Those who infringe upon the above three main points should be resisted with the strength of the entire nation. The deduction of this theory is that they regard Manchuria and Mongolia as Japanese territory. Taking advantage of the opportunity of the Shenyang Incident, they should use the military strength of the entire nation to eradicate the "Chinese" forces in this land and simultaneously settle accounts for the incompetence of "Shidehara Diplomacy." This kind of argument is currently very influential.

Secondly, it is to urge "China" to respect treaty rights and interests. On the other hand, it should connect with friendly nations without placing Japan in a state of isolation. In other words, after the demise of the "Anglo-Japanese Alliance," Japan has lost countries with harmonious relations in the recent world. At the time of the Shenyang Incident's outbreak, it is even more necessary to connect with a friendly nation that can support Japan's Manchurian and Mongolian policy. This public opinion heavily criticizes the Japanese foreign affairs authorities for their lack of effort, or at least criticizes the inadequacy of their efforts. This is the general and common opinion.

Thirdly, this proposition is also a representative of ruthless and vicious military personnel. They believe that the Japanese foreign affairs authorities' "proposal to demand respect for treaties and confirmation of rights and interests" is a mistake. To put it bluntly, Manchuria and Mongolia have a very deep relationship with Japan. Whoever invades Manchuria and Mongolia should be punished. The world's interference in Manchuria and Mongolia should be regarded as an enemy. Therefore, this Shenyang Incident is not merely "China's" disrespect for treaties; it is simply "China's" attack on Japan's ideal territory. Manchuria and Mongolia should deal with it with the final determination.

Fourthly, this wonderful theory comes from the Japanese diplomatic circle. It believes that the major issue of handling the Shenyang Incident should be addressed by a specialized committee of the League of Nations. The committee should examine a reasonable method for resolving the Manchurian and Mongolian issues. In the end, this solution is to adopt the "mandate system," and under this mandate system, establish the future fate of our Northeast.

Fifthly, this is an observation from the perspective of a socialist. They believe that the current protection of Japan's rights and interests in Manchuria and Mongolia is unreasonable. They say that although Japan's investment in Manchuria and Mongolia has reached 1.5 billion yen, the majority of it is investment by the Zaibatsu (financial conglomerates). The so-called protection of Manchurian and Mongolian rights and interests only results in an increase in the profits of a few bourgeois individuals. Under these circumstances, Japan absolutely has no need to sacrifice 100,000 lives or 200,000 units of national expenditure. However, if capitalist Japan collapses and socialist Japan is born, then it would be worthwhile to fight a decisive battle for Manchuria and Mongolia. The protection of Manchurian and Mongolian rights and interests under socialism is the lifeline of all Japanese citizens. This theory is relatively fresh.

Among the above five representative public opinions, regardless of the speaker's position or whether the remarks criticize the current Japanese government, there seems to be a consistent argument for "maintaining Manchuria and Mongolia." It also very clearly implies the maturity of Japan's second phase of continental policy. The recent outbreak of the Shenyang Incident is merely a phenomenon of labor pains during pregnancy. The long night is endless, and the future is truly unbearable to imagine. Although the Third International Council has already been convened, we dare to assert that there will be no justice in the international community. Self-preservation depends on self-strengthening. Japan can continuously invade the mainland, but can China continuously seek help from the League of Nations? (November 18th)

Taiwan 55

Rogue Elements Disrupting Fuzhou Conspiracy

Now Completely Exposed

Fuzhou Correspondence: Since the Japanese warship "Maru-shima" sailed into the inner harbor of Fuzhou, the social atmosphere in Minyuan has suddenly become tense. Adding to this, for several consecutive days, seven bombs were discovered on the side of Cangshan Mountain near the South Gate of the city, and a fire broke out in a Taiwanese opium den in Lane Kuai Li within the city. Rumors arose for a time, and the people were panicked. Military and police agencies also tightened security. Traffic was cut off at 10:00 PM each night, and the situation was particularly serious. Later, after investigation by the authorities, it was discovered that Taiwanese rogue elements were causing trouble from within, hoping to cause conflict between China and Japan, so that they could take advantage of the opportunity to profit. Therefore, they falsely reported to the Japanese consul that Chinese student militias were planning to attack the consulate. On the one hand, they reported to the Chinese military and police that Japanese people and Taiwanese people had organized a riot team to plot to throw bombs, set fires, and rob, etc. Both sides believed it to be true. The "Maru-shima" warship immediately removed its gun covers and set up machine guns. The consulate then turned off the lights at night and dispatched Japanese police officers to cooperate with sailors to patrol around the inside and outside of the building. Important Japanese people also prepared to leave Min. Seeing that the Japanese side was taking such action, and confirming the bomb incident at Nanmendou and the fire incident at Lane Kuai Li, our military and police also greatly increased security. It was not until the Japanese consul saw that Chinese students were attending classes as usual without any disturbance, and also heard rumors that Taiwanese people, such as a Mr. Liu, a Mr. Li, and a Mr. Ke, were spreading rumors and deceiving the public, that he realized that he had been deceived. He immediately sent Mr. Liu back to his hometown, and Mr. Li and Mr. Ke also hid and dared not come out. The conspiracy of the rogue elements was thus completely exposed. (November 27th)

Central and National Government Memorial Week 57

At 9:00 AM on November 30th, the Central Party Headquarters held a memorial week in the Great Hall of the Central Party Headquarters. Central Committee members Dai Kui Sheng, Chen Guofu, Shao Yuanchong, and others, as well as staff from various departments and bureaus, and guests, totaling about 500 people, attended. Chairman Chen Guofu presided over the ceremony. After the ceremony, Shao Yuanchong gave a report, which stated that China's internal continuous disputes have led to political division and the weakening of national power. All construction cannot be carried out. In addition, discipline has been abandoned, and the people lack a spirit of abiding by the law, resulting in the instability of social order. In education, it has failed to adapt to the environment of the country and the people and the needs of the new era, and measures have not been appropriate, causing the people's patriotic psychology and movement to sometimes fail to fully conform to the norm. Scientific knowledge has not been fully developed. Therefore, imperialists are using our country's weaknesses to intensify their aggressive policies, causing continuous crises for our country and nation. The most inhumane Japanese imperialism, based on its consistent traditional policy of aggression against China, has recently become rampant, and its ambitions are fully exposed. It uses various insidious means to deceive the League of Nations and confuse the truth, so that international justice cannot be fully upheld. At this time of crisis for our country,

if we do not awaken and urgently catch up to correct past mistakes and remedy past shortcomings, then danger is imminent, and the consequences will be unimaginable. Therefore, when the Fourth Plenary Session was convened, it unanimously sought to realize unity within the party based on the principles of fraternity and sincerity, create a unified country through unity within the party, use political momentum to consolidate the foundation of the country, and then make every effort to cope with the national crisis, use extremely effective methods to eliminate all obstacles, resist armed aggression, and resolve the current major crisis. On the side of our party, we should absolutely take responsibility. I especially hope that our entire nation will share this goal, proceed in unison, and take disciplined and efficient actions in the midst of common struggles, abide by the law, and not overstep boundaries. We must also know that China's weakness is not the result of one morning and one evening. The fundamental reason lies in the lack of daily education and the slow progress of scientific knowledge. The powerful foundation of any imperialist or socialist country in the world lies not only in military and political power, but in the development of economic power through scientific power, so that the country becomes rich and strong day by day. Therefore, we should pay close attention to the basic dangers of our country and work together to find a path to resolve them, so that we can have hope of resisting foreign aggression and prevent the recurrence of bullying and oppression in the future, etc. After the report, the meeting adjourned at 10:00 AM.

At 10:00 AM on the same morning, the National Government held the Prime Minister's Memorial Week. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, as well as the heads of various Yuan, Ministries, and Commissions, including Dai Chuanxian, Shao Yuanchong, Lin Sen, He Yingqin, Zhu Peide, Song Ziwen, Ma Fuxiang, Wang Boqun, Yang Shuzhuang, Li Shuhua, Wu Tiecheng, Chen Bulei, Chen Shaokuan, Gu Zhenglun, Wu Siyu, Zhou Yawei, etc., as well as all staff from the three offices of civil affairs, military affairs, and accounting, attended. Chairman Chiang led the ceremony as usual. Then, President Dai gave a report, stating that the current diplomatic situation is urgent and the country is in danger. The ancients once said that a country that has no external enemies will always perish. If we want to cope with difficulties, we must not have other new plans or work. We only need to abide by the Prime Minister's teachings, earnestly believe that everyone should double their efforts in their profession. The government's responsibility is not only to be the public servant of the people but also to be the leader of the nation. It must lead the people to seek common construction, protect the foundation of the country, and overcome difficulties, etc. After the report, the meeting adjourned.

Fengxian 58

The Fifth District Public Office Plans Funding for the Shiniu Tuan Culvert. Yesterday, for the sake of planning the funding for the construction of the culvert at Shiniu Tuan, a meeting of enthusiastic people from the county was convened at Qianjiaqiao to discuss and decide on the following: (1) The number of insufficient funds, in addition to the 500 yuan subsidy from the property disposal office, will be borne separately by the employed households. Declaration of New Silk Reeling Method: The All Circles Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association previously received a letter from the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Association, informing them that the Wuxi Minfeng Silk Factory hired Japanese slaves as technicians to manage the machines, used Japanese goods on the machines without authorization, and manufactured silkworm seed Japanese goods equipment. As for silk reeling, it adopts the world's latest methods. A Korean, Li Guanghua, was hired as a technician. Although the term was not over after the Ten Thousand Incident, he was immediately dismissed and left Xizhi long ago. As for imitating the Japanese silk reeling method, it is a world scientific public matter. Industry is changing rapidly every day, and it should be encouraged. Fearing that misunderstandings would occur, a letter has been sent yesterday to declare this.

It was resolved to be punished by parading in the streets, which will be implemented immediately.

Jurong Giant Bandit Arrested and Escorted to Zhenjiang: According to a report from the Jurong Hu Zhen Ning Sui Jing Sub-district Command, the Jurong household bandit Zhu Shitong (i.e., Zhu Tieshan) repeatedly committed theft cases and fled to Shanghai. Officers were sent to Shanghai to submit a document to the civil service hall, requesting arrest. They happened to encounter Zhu at the corner of Xinxin Bridge on Damalu in the French Concession. They arrested and escorted him to the Zhenjiang Court for interrogation. He confessed without denial.

The Civil Affairs Office Continues to Handle Ship Registration: The Jiangsu Provincial Civil Affairs Office stated that the previous temporary measures for clearing and inspecting ships in various counties, which were ordered by the Jiangsu Province Clearing Township Bureau, are now outdated. Referencing the previous temporary measures, seven new ship continuation registration measures have been formulated. After being passed by the Provincial Government Committee meeting, an order was sent to the county governments yesterday to comply with and handle the matter.

Salt Smugglers Colluding with Bandits to Harass Northern Jiangsu Counties: Recently, large numbers of bandits, using the names of famine victims, have been taking the opportunity to loot. According to reports, these bandits are mostly salt smugglers from counties such as Yancheng and Funing, who have joined forces with bandits to harass the local area. The Jiangsu Provincial Government yesterday specially instructed the county heads of Northern Jiangsu to quickly dispatch police teams to conduct thorough searches, increase vigilance, and block and strike.

Nantong 62

Details of the Datda Steamer Robbery at Liuyu: The Datda Steamship Company's Dade steamer, which was en route from Shanghai to the Upper Yangtze, passed through Nantong Tianshenggang at 12:00 AM on the 27th. At approximately 1:00 AM on the 28th, when it reached the Liuyu river surface in Taixing County, it was suddenly robbed by bandits. The search and robbery lasted for two hours, and no passengers were spared. The details of the robbery are recorded below: When the Dade steamer departed from Shanghai on the 27th, bandits disguised as passengers had already purchased tickets and boarded the ship. Later, when passing through Tongru, more bandits joined. When the ship reached Liuyu, a rowboat came from the north bank, first using a flashlight to signal. The bandits on the ship each took out pistols and started the attack, ordering the workers in the engine room to stop the ship. Together with the bandits on the rowboat, there were more than 50 people, who searched the ticket office and cargo compartments. The bandits all wore Red Army insignia and carried firearms. The ticket office was searched three times in a row, but only a little more than 400 yuan was robbed. They fired shots in the cargo hold to show off their power. Because they did not get any cash, they focused on the passengers. No passenger in the officer's cabin was spared. Their suitcases were robbed, and they were all looted. Only a passenger surnamed Zhu lost 400 yuan, and a female passenger's dowry jewelry, which she had prepared in Shanghai, was a relatively large amount. The rest were all small amounts of money and small pieces of jewelry. The copper coins carried by the passengers in the general cabin were also robbed. Many of the passengers' clothes and shoes were also stripped off. Five large rolls of cloth were robbed from the cargo hold. Because the rowboat was already full of suitcases, two rolls were returned. A bag of rice was also robbed. At 3:30 AM, they shouted, boarded the rowboat, and escaped. An insignia with the words "Red Army Division No. 2020" was left on the ship. According to statistics, the total loss for the company and passengers was approximately more than 6,000 yuan.

Disaster Relief Center Continues to Operate: The Jiangbei disaster relief center established in Nantong was scheduled to close at the end of the month and send the disaster victims back to their hometowns due to a lack of funds. On the 29th, an order was received from the province, approving the allocation of funds from the Provincial Relief Council to continue operating.

Yangzhou 63

Regular Resumption of Operations of the Yangzhou-Zhenjiang Automobile: The Yangzhou Long-Distance Automobile Company has been suspended for four months since the canal breach caused by the water. The company has suffered considerable losses, and travelers have also experienced inconvenience. Therefore, the company has repeatedly tried to first automatically block the riverbank near the road south of the canal, then use pumps to drain the accumulated water on the road, and finally provide funds to the disaster victims residing on the unflooded road and persuade them to relocate. After operating for several weeks, it has been completed. It is now heard that traffic will resume on December 1st.

Daliuzhuang Robbery Injures People: Liu Huailin, a resident of Daliuzhuang in the west township, was attacked by a group of more than a dozen bandits, who held box guns and pistols, entered his house by climbing over the roof from his neighbor's house, lit incense to force him to hand over his property, and suffered burns in many places. At the same time, they rushed to each room to search and rob silver jewelry worth about 100 yuan before fleeing with shouts.

Rugao 64

Rural Residents Oppose the Wine Tax Craze: Recently, residents in the western township of Juegang opposed Chen Jinshan's collection of home-brewed wine tax and posted leaflets, sounded gongs to gather people, and agreed to go to the Cha'an Temple on the 24th to burn incense and swear an oath to unanimously refuse to collect the wine tax. The township head discovered the matter and reported it to the Mao District head for handling. After receiving the report, the Mao District head believed that it was illegal to sound gongs and gather people during the winter defense period. Therefore, he took the leader, Lu Wangdai, to the place to guide him and avoid trouble. Unexpectedly, on the afternoon of the 24th, hundreds of residents in the western township gathered and surged to the district office, destroying most of the seating in the discussion hall and the glass in the windows. They also beat more than ten guards. When Director Yin of the Public Security Bureau's detachment went to maintain order, his head was also hit by a shoulder pole. Fortunately, the section chief and district office staff persuaded them, and the township residents dispersed after Cloud returned Lu Wangdai. The district office is currently investigating the leader for prosecution.
