Matters Discussed (1) How to stipulate the powers of this committee: The general meeting decided that this committee belongs to the representative assembly, but it does not comply with the organizational law of the assembly and conflicts with the executive committee. It was resolved that this committee shall decide to request the next representative assembly to amend it, and this committee belongs to the executive committee. (2) Before the powers of this committee are determined, it is only responsible for preparing for the general review. After the preparation, it will be handled by the military training department, and no other discussions will be held. Resolution passed. (3) The location of the general review will be contacted by Datong and Liangjiang and reported within two days. Resolution passed. (4) Selected personnel will be designated to prepare the general review plan. Those elected were Jiaotong University, Jiaotong University, and Liangjiang University. (5) The outline and date of the plan will be determined after the location of the general review is determined. The current six points of the content are determined first: (A) Mobilizing infantry, (B) Transportation, (C) Venue layout, (D) Organization of the Volunteer Army Rescue Team, (E) Review procedure, (F) Budget. Resolution passed (6) The source of funds will be obtained from the executive committee.

Mrs. Maudie's "Championship Competition" 98

The arrival of Mrs. Maudie, the world tennis queen from the United States, is a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity. The people of Shanghai can be said to have good fortune. It is published to the readers during Mrs. Maudie's visit to China. It has begun to be published in the sixth issue published last Saturday. In addition, Zeng Yanhua's football masterpiece "Football Strategy" will also be published in this issue. The national public must read and subscribe. The annual subscription fee is two yuan and five jiao in China and six yuan abroad, including postage. The address of the publishing house is No. 40 Zhenhua Lane, Marang Road, French Concession, Shanghai.

Words Remembered from Dai Liang 99

— Yan Zi

After the Xianfeng period of the Qing Dynasty, overseas vassals such as Korea, Ryukyu, and Vietnam were all annexed by strong neighbors. China was unable to prevent it. The Sino-French War of Jiashen was caused by Vietnam. Vietnam bordered Guangxi. In the Battle of Lang Son, Governor Feng Zicai of Guangxi was the first to bear the brunt. He tried his best to resist the invaders but failed repeatedly. Later, Wang, with the help of his drunk friends, captured the French army transporting the equipment. Because of the lack of ammunition in the front line, the front line was defeated. At that time, the French Navy Admiral Courbet was shot and killed by a naval student in the Battle of Mawei. The military prestige was greatly reduced. Each court official had thoughts on how to solve the situation, negotiating peace with France. The public uproar grew. Chen Zhefu, a candidate who participated in the Japanese government, and a junior official, followed the imperial commissioner Xu Chengzuyuan back to China. He deeply hated the ways of the Japanese. At the time of the Meiji Restoration, he strongly advocated self-improvement and reform. Japan had already swallowed Ryukyu and was trying to蚕食Korea, so he already despised China and wanted to make a difference. Chen enumerated the crimes of Japan. He requested to move the victorious army from Lang Son to征征 Japan and question Ryukyu, the whole article in more than 2,000 words. It was widely circulated at one time, but the Grand Council of Minister Xu Yongyi knew well the minds of the two palaces (Empress Dowager was纵情 and enjoying herself while building the Summer Palace.) The emperor did not express an opinion. The court thought the young boy was wrong to start border wars. The emperor ignored the suggestion, missing a good opportunity. The treacherous officials have misled the country for thousands of years, making people feel infinite emotion. Moreover, there was a famous division, and the division was strong. If at that time, according to Zhefu's intention, the army was transferred eastward, then Ryukyu could be restored, Korea would not be destroyed, and how could the root cause of the Sino-Japanese War be caused, and the fence would be completely removed.

Qian Hezhou's Defense Against Japanese Pirates 100

— Xi Xiaohua

During the Jiajing period of the Ming Dynasty, Japanese pirates disturbed Jiangyin. At that time, the magistrate Qian Hezhou, a native of Jingzhou, was 26 years old. He defended and resisted with Yang Ku, Xu Rong of Qingqiao, and the righteous servant Zhu Gui. He died for his country. His loyalty and courage are enough to influence future generations. At that time, it was the 33rd year of Jiajing. There was a Japanese police in Cheng when the Spring Festival was celebrated. Only the East Gate was left for entry and exit, and the other three gates were closed to prevent changes. In the evening, foreigners flocked into the city. The gate was congested, and 47 people were trampled to death. On April 28, the Japanese suddenly arrived at Qingqiao from Huangsipu. Xu Rong had already blocked the port. Qian Gong ordered him to lead the militia to repel them. Another group of Japanese came from the south. Rong returned to the army to meet the attack north of Yangxu, a place called Sanguantang. The thief's crossbow was fired indiscriminately, and the soldiers had no armor. So he left. The righteous servant Chen Xu Rong was only spared. The village was terribly burned and killed by the thieves. Xu Rong's house was also burned. Xu Rong once wrote a poem to commemorate it: "Holding his wife and children in front of the horse, everywhere he frowned and mourned for the dead family. The huts were burnt to ashes, and the roads were lost and his eyes were faint. The old site was desolate, and the spring swallow was injured, and the bleak remains filled the late crows. Looking up at the desolation, the hatred was infinite, and from where to enjoy life."

In the 34th year of Jiajing, more than 3,000 Japanese pirates from Changshu joined together and divided from the river. The pirates attacked Qingjiang and landed at Caigang. Qian Gong, the county magistrate, was ordered by Wang Chonggu, the commander of the army, to lead his troops to aid Jing, but he returned in a hurry after receiving the news. The Japanese had already arrived at the bridge, but they failed to attack the city. They retreated to defend the Chaqing sluice gate (now called Nanzha Town) and plundered day and night. The smoke and fire connected the sky, and nearly 10,000 villagers entered the city to take refuge. Qian Gong was furious and wanted to fight, but the county soldiers were no more than 400 people, plus 1,000 soldiers from Guangdong and Guangxi. So, on June 23, he left the city to fight. First, the soldiers from Guangdong and Guangxi were indulgent. Qian punished them according to the law. They fled when they met the bandits. Qian alone fought against the enemy with more than 50 of his personal soldiers. Yang Cheng, a personal soldier, hated the Japanese for their slaughter and was especially brave. Qian encountered the Japanese and fought at Jiuliwan, commonly known as Mopandun (now outside the South Gate). The terrain was dangerous and the horse fell. Yang Cheng hurriedly exchanged his horse for him. Suddenly, the Japanese bandits ambushed in the grass and stabbed Qian Gong with knives. He was stabbed several times, but he still fought the bandits with all his strength. The Japanese pirates stabbed Qian with spears, and his body was as broken as mud. More than 20 righteous soldiers died with Qian. Xue Jia, a villager, cried and buried him among the dead soldiers.

Evening Two Days Before Zhimo's Accident 101

— He Tianjian

Zhimo is dead. Life is a busy pursuit, and every day we inevitably move towards death. Death is unavoidable, so why should death cause such grief? However, the way death touches people's emotions and impacts talent determines whether it is heavier than Mount Tai or lighter than a feather. Zhimo did not die in a national crisis, nor in pursuit of academic endeavors, nor due to other matters related to society or personal affairs, but in a plane crash. He died without deserving it, his life lighter than a feather. This causes emotional distress and is something Zhimo himself, even in death, would not have wished for. Therefore, people lament his death, regretting the loss of his talent and lamenting his misfortune. Zhimo's scholarship and talent are well-known to everyone; I will not repeat them here. After Zhimo returned to the south, I met him at the Modern Painting Exhibition. He seemed very pleased with his wife, Madam Xiaoman's, paintings and expressed his gratitude to me. In reality, Madam Xiaoman was already quite knowledgeable about painting. I was merely providing some consultation. Moreover, the consultation time was quite short. How could it be considered instruction? When we parted, we made arrangements for a crab feast. Zhimo had brought a basket of crabs from his home in Xiashi. Xiashi is known for its crabs. A day later, I visited his residence. Zhimo entered from outside, shook my hand, and greeted me warmly. Soon, we sat down to eat crabs. We enjoyed the creamy roe and plump meat. Some at the table were not skilled at eating them, so Zhimo taught them how to dissect them. During the meal, we talked about his experience on a Ford plane between Beijing and Ping. He said that north of the Yellow River, the fields below looked dark purple, and south of the river, the fields looked red, very smooth and clean. The layout of the fields and paths was like a chessboard, very orderly. As for the cities, towns, and places where people gathered, they were like ant colonies or swarms of gnats, busily working. At this point, he suddenly sighed and said, "I never imagined that in this small area, there would be so much worry and joy." I said, "The 'Autumn Floods' chapter of Zhuangzi emphasizes this three times. Why should I be surprised?" Madam Xiaoman, seeing that Zhimo's eye condition had not yet fully recovered, advised him to eat less. Zhimo then said to me, "I am very fond of this food. When I was in Beiping, my eye condition was caused by it. Now it is almost recovered." He then encouraged me and others to eat more. I had already eaten dinner, so I ate only two. Zhimo then drank three cups of wine, his spirits high. He got up and began to sing loudly and dance like a myna. This was the happiest I had ever seen him. Wu Ziguan, entrusted by Li, wanted Zhimo's calligraphy, which he had asked for three years ago. Taking this opportunity, he asked Zhimo to write. Zhimo, in high spirits, wrote the "Fisherman" chapter by Qu Yuan. After finishing, it looked just like Zheng Haizang's work. It was late, so I shook hands and said goodbye. Zhimo said, "I will only be gone for three weeks and will return soon. We will see each other soon." We said our goodbyes and I left. The next morning, I also took a car back to Xi. Alas, who knew that this half-night of joyful conversation would be the second-to-last night of Zhimo's life? Alas, I did not have a deep, long-lasting friendship with Zhimo, but we had been connected spiritually for years. I saw his wife, Madam Xiaoman, more often when she studied landscape painting with me, but that was only in the first half of the year. Since May, I had been on leave for three or four days due to being busy and the hot weather. Last month, I returned from leave and met with Zhimo again. This meeting was the last one. Alas. Zhimo, lamenting the lack of excellent works in the history of Chinese painting, had asked me to compile a history of Chinese painters. He had even compared arm strength with me; Zhimo was also a martial arts practitioner. Alas, Zhimo! Alas, Zhimo!

Mourning Xu Zhimo 102

— Jian Mang

At the end of a rugged world, poets are destined to be buried in the sky. If he transforms into a crane in Liaodong in another life, he will weep at the setting sun and the red blood of war.

Transforming into a Peng bird, flying all over the sky, his ambition was never small in his youth. Who would have thought he would become a feathered immortal today? From now on, he will not return to the human world. (Zhimo, in his anthology, published an article titled "Wanting to Fly," in which he described how he deeply admired the soaring of vultures over the top of pagodas in his childhood.)

A Song for You 103

— Lao Man

Shakespeare has a poem titled "A Song for You." I once translated its meaning into five-character prose and published it in the "Saturday Weekly." It says, "I sing for the love of you, not for the sake of the song itself. The song may disappear, but its memory remains in your heart. If you remember me, my song will always be joyful. When you leave me, it will be a source of comfort. In the brightly lit happy night, we forget to go home in laughter and talk. I sing for you again, and we are comfortable tonight. There is no loneliness anymore, as if we are close to each other. I sing for the love of you; please do not forget my feelings." The poem has a wonderful artistic conception, but unfortunately, I lack the ability to translate it into rhyming verse.

The other day, I happened to go to the movies and heard the singing of Ms. Ruth Chatterton, which resembled Shakespeare's song. A famous person and a famous song, coming from the beautiful mouth of a lady, made it even more charming. I usually do not like talking movies because I always feel that I cannot understand the European accents completely. However, in the love songs in sound movies, I often find one or two good verses. How moving a song is!

Since ancient times, our country has spared no effort in studying music and song. Romantic anecdotes and rumors are often spread through songs. In unofficial histories, there are many old stories of singing venues, which are widely circulated. Recently, the Mingxing Film Company released sound films such as "Such is Paradise" and "Sing-song Girl Red Peony," and the Tianyi Film Company released the sound film "Spring Colors of the Singing Venue." All of them use the singing venue as a decoration. What a pity is that the performance and emotions are not fully integrated.

Recently, Ms. Xuan Jinglin told me that she had recently starred in a new film by Mingxing Film Company, "Eternal Farewell of a Beautiful Woman." The film is silent and directed by the great director Zheng Zhengqiu. The female lead, named Yu Ren, is a singer. Although we cannot hear the songs in the film, we can sense the tension of the plot and the intensity of the emotions, making it an unprecedented work among domestic films and giving the audience a feeling that "silence is better than sound at this time."

Everyone knows that Ms. Xuan is good at singing. However, in the film "Eternal Farewell of a Beautiful Woman," she does not move people with her singing but with her delicate expressions. Perhaps it is like what Shakespeare said in his poem: "The song may disappear, but its memory remains in your heart."

Jue Lin Returns 104

— Juan

Last summer, Mr. Fen exhibited his calligraphy and seal carvings at Jue Lin. At that time, many people gathered to praise him. Juan also wrote an article about it. Now Mr. Fen has released new works and is sharing them with enthusiasts again. How grand! Mr. Fen is not yet forty years old but is proficient in all four forms of calligraphy. He is especially excellent in seal script and clerical script. For example, the five-foot couplet "With downward eyes, ninety thousand miles, sitting and watching the eighteen dukes," his style is similar to Yi Bingshou. The five-foot coral paper inscription pair, copied from Qian Shilan, has no current bad habits of recklessness but has a natural air. The five-foot Zhongtang inscription of Yue Wu Mu's "Man Jiang Hong" in its entirety also shows skilled workmanship and is completed in one go. I love his four-foot vertical scroll even more, the seal script "Three Qin Records People's Ballads," which is refined. Gentle but not flattering, clear but not stained. I stroked and admired it, reluctant to let it go. At that time, Mr. Wang Xishen also arrived and especially appreciated his "There is still a thatched roof to lodge swallows, how can there be no half-grain to reach the fish in the pond," saying that it was the saying of a benevolent person, but he did not know which family this poem came from. I asked Mr. Fen, who said it was his own work. He is indeed skilled in poetry. Many exquisite works were displayed in the venue. They imitated the Qin and Han dynasties and were extremely wonderful. Xishen bought two copies and left. I also could not stay for long due to errands and disappointedly returned, but my mind's eye still seemed to see the flower-paper seals, shining red among the three true and six cursive scripts.

World Short News 105

— Hai Ke

Bicycle City: According to a recent survey, the bicycle, which has long been disliked, seems to be becoming popular again. This is because the production of bicycle factories has increased dramatically compared to the past seven or eight years. Although it is rare to see bicycles in several major cities these years, there are still some towns that are known as bicycle cities. For example, Bedford in England is the most famous bicycle city. The number of bicycles per capita is the highest in all of England. This is probably because the surrounding terrain is flat. Because there are many cyclists, general stores have special bicycle parking facilities to provide customers with convenience. In addition to Bedford, almost everyone in Copenhagen, the capital of Denmark, rides a bicycle.

The Hague is the same. These two places can be truly called bicycle cities. In Berlin, the capital of Germany, the streets are also filled with bicycles when workers go to and from work. There are workshops in factories outside the city to accommodate thousands of bicycles because it is the cheapest and easiest way for people to get around.

Taiwan Reporter's Hatred of National Subjugation (Part 1) 106

— Ms. Ye Hua

The first territory of our country to be forcibly occupied by the neighboring Japanese was Ryukyu, followed by Taiwan. In 1895, the Treaty of Shimonoseki was signed. Li Jingfang, under orders, met with the Japanese General Kabayama and transferred Taiwan. From then on, Taiwan fell to a foreign race, never to recover. Yesterday, Mr. Zhang from the Tainan newspaper went to England via Shanghai. The Shanghai colleagues of the China Newspaper Society held a farewell dinner. During the dinner, they talked about the extremely difficult situation of Taiwanese newspapers and the utmost efforts they made. They sobbed and wept, unable to control themselves. Therefore, I recorded one or two of them. How can it only be like Lu Jia's "New Words"?

Newspapers as Tools: This year's census shows that Taiwan currently has a population of 4.56 million. There are four daily newspapers and four weekly newspapers, all of which are founded by Japanese people as semi-official and semi-private ventures. The one in Taipei is called Taiwan Daily News, with a daily circulation of 15,000, the best in Taiwan. There is Taiwan News in Taichung, with a daily circulation of 8,000. Tainan has Tainan New News, with a daily circulation of 10,000. Dong Taiwan News is located in Hualienjiang, with a daily sale of 3,000. The weekly newspaper in Taipei is Jingshi New News, with 5,000 copies each time. South Japan New News has 3,000 copies at a time. Showa New News and Nan Ying New News each have 2,000 copies. Xin Gao New News is located in Keelung, with a weekly sale of 6,000 copies. The above newspapers are all tools of the Japanese government. Every word and sentence obeys the orders of the Japanese. If the government calls a deer a horse, then all the newspapers will call a deer a horse. A piece of news released in the evening will be seen in all the newspapers the next morning, and not a single word can be changed. On Chinese issues, they often criticize and slander, turning black into white.

Daily Restrictions: In addition to the above eight official newspapers, the Japanese Osaka Asahi and other major newspapers are also imported, about several thousand copies a day. Taiwanese people resent the entry of compatriots into misery and the lack of freedom of speech. They gathered gentlemen and people of vision to form Taiwan Xinmin Co., Ltd., regarding China as their motherland and calling themselves overseas Taiwanese Chinese. They raised 370,000 yuan to engage in national movement, allocating 100,000 yuan to edit Taiwan Xinmin Daily, secretly advocating national revolution and awakening national consciousness. The newspaper became a thorn in the side of the Japanese, who spared no effort in trampling and destroying it. However, the newspaper did not yield but painstakingly maintained itself for ten years, with a circulation of nearly 10,000. It repeatedly wanted to change to a daily newspaper but was always prohibited. This is because newspapers must obtain a permit from the Japanese authorities before they can be published daily without hindrance.

Rotary Club Storytelling

Country Bumpkin Visits Shanghai Again (33) 107

— Bao Tianxiao

The country bumpkin was stunned to see the chartered cars on the road coming and going like shuttles. He not only saw that those "female Zhuges" were all holding strange and colorful feather fans in their hands, but also saw that they were all carrying small leather wallets. The country bumpkin suspected what was in these girls' wallets. Could they all be female students going to school? But what kind of books are they studying at night? Unless Shanghai has opened a lot of midnight girls' schools. Otherwise, are they all female shop assistants, carrying those wallets, going out to collect debts? But sitting in such fancy cars, these debt collectors are a bit too wealthy.

There was another chartered car passing by the country bumpkin, and he felt a flash of light in front of him. It turned out that there were many electric lights on the chartered car. The country bumpkin counted the electric lights on the chartered car, and there were exactly seven of them. The country bumpkin suddenly had an idea:

"That's right! That's right! This is a performer! Her name is Seven Lamps. I've heard people from Shanghai say that there's a female actor named Seven Lamps. I didn't know why she was called Seven Lamps? Now look at this car, isn't it clearly fitted with seven lamps? This must be Seven Lamps without a doubt."

The country bumpkin looked around. He forgot to ask the rickshaw puller to find his nephew and just walked around aimlessly. The more he walked, the more lively it became. He saw a place where trams were connected in all directions, red and green lights were flashing, and cars were bumper to bumper. The heads of these cars touching the butts of the cars in front of them. The heads of the cars in front were touching the butts of the cars further in front. The perfume of the beautiful girls in the rickshaws and the sweaty smell of the coolies pulling the rickshaws were intertwined, forming a kind of fragrant and stinky odor. The strangest thing was an Indian black carbon gentleman, standing high in the bucket of a flagpole in the center of the road. The country bumpkin thought: He is enjoying the cool breeze in that place, he is truly in his element! He is truly in his element!

Recently, a new type of red electric light, with red, green, and yellow colors, has become popular. When it gets dark, they shine in various colors, and everywhere is lit up. What company are they? What store name is it? You can see it from afar. The red letters are bordered with green, and the yellow letters are bordered with red. The country bumpkin was stunned as he looked. He just kept looking from house to house, and he saw a large building, and there were two red electric lights, very large, shining on the top, which said: "Anti-Occupy."

When the country bumpkin saw it, he felt anger rising from his heart and courage from his liver. He clenched his fists and rushed toward the store, shouting in his mouth:

"Beat! Beat! Beat! Beat that traitor to death! Beat that national scum to death! Beat that cold-blooded animal to death!"

Finance 108

Gold Price Exceeds 700 Taels

A Sharp Increase of 30 Taels and Nine Qian: Yesterday, the gold price suddenly peaked. The storm was still calm, and the advance was sharp but hesitant, resulting in a large rise and small pullback. Throughout the day, there were speculators covering their positions by three to four taels, and in the end, the price rose sharply by more than thirty taels. It rose from the morning, mainly because the silver price fell and, more importantly, because the Japanese troops suddenly retreated from Jinzhou, leading to rising confidence. As a result, many short positions were covered, and large players actively competed to buy. Moreover, foreign exchange was tight, causing the gold price to soar without obstruction, breaking through the 700-tael mark. Subsequently, a new high price of 707.5 taels appeared, and then many sellers seemed to emerge, as those who could profit had already sold. The exchange rate also leveled off slightly, causing the price to drop by ten taels. Later, it returned above 700 taels.

Opening Jump and Subsequent Rise: The price rose by 15.2 qian immediately after opening, reaching 684.5 taels. The near-term silver price remained unchanged from the previous day, while the far-term price rose slightly by one-sixteenth. The silver price fell by one-fourth. As the situation turned calmer, only the Dalian gang was slightly bearish, and the price retreated to 84 taels. In a short time, the price surged by more than ten taels, and Dadecheng, Daxing, Yonghengchang, and Yongyuanmao and others actively competed to buy. The exchange rate also strengthened. It was estimated that the British gold price at the bank was initially 19.8125, then 75, and then rose to 95.5 taels. Securities 112

Government Bonds Suddenly Surge 113

All Bonds Except 96 Suspended from Trading 114

Yesterday (the 30th), trading in all government bonds at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange was extremely sparse. Futures trading was suspended as soon as the market opened in the morning. At the opening, market sentiment was positive, and buying was strong. The disparity between supply and demand caused prices to soar, leading to a suspension of trading in almost all bonds. Except for the Customs Bonds, which were not offered, the 96 bonds were about one yuan away from the limit price. All other bonds had already risen by four yuan compared to the closing price last Saturday. Consequently, only 96 government bonds were traded at the close of the market. Due to the additional margin requirement, trading only resumed after 4 pm, and only in 96 bonds. Even with the suspended bonds, off-market trading continued. The off-market prices remained high due to strong demand, rising considerably above the suspended prices. It was reported that the highest off-market price for Salt Bonds reached 49 yuan in the morning, a level rarely seen recently. The price surge eased slightly in the afternoon, but the actual prices were still about three yuan higher than the suspended prices. The sudden surge in bond prices is attributed to the withdrawal of Japanese troops and the turning of diplomatic circumstances, as well as the exchange's efforts to maintain the market by limiting new sales. The bond market appears promising, and market sentiment has improved. However, it is still too early to be overly optimistic, as the future depends on diplomatic developments. Nevertheless, the securities market has stabilized after this rebound, preventing the instability seen previously. It is expected that today's prices will likely continue to rise, but not as drastically as yesterday's surge and suspension of trading. There were no spot transactions yesterday, and the one-month futures contract did not open. The December futures contract totaled 2,455,000 yuan. Off-market transactions were based on suspended prices, and the amount was not large. The whole six bonds opened and were immediately suspended, with no transactions.

Strict Military and Police Precautions in the City 149

Still Under Martial Law Last Night 150

The military and police authorities in the city, due to rumors that Japanese ronin are colluding with bandits and recruiting unemployed hooligans to disrupt public order, declared special martial law to maintain public order, starting the night before last. Zhabei was the most severely affected. Martial law was declared from 6 pm yesterday until 6 am the next morning. All police officers from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, including those from the district, branch, sub-stations, and police stations, were fully armed. All police officers from the police brigade were also fully deployed and checked pedestrians. Soldiers from the first tax police regiment stationed at the Huzhou Guildhall in Zhabei were armed and on guard, but this was temporary. Martial law will be lifted once the rumors subside. In the Public Concession, the Yangshupu Huishan and other police stations have increased the deployment of a large number of armed Chinese and Western detectives, creating an invisible martial law. This is because the areas under their jurisdiction are where the Japanese live.

Important Remarks by Zhang Qun 151

A reporter from the China East News Agency visited Mayor Zhang yesterday to inquire about various issues such as public security in the city. He gave detailed answers as follows:

Reasons for Martial Law: Mr. Zhang first stated that the reason for the special martial law in the city the night before last was due to frequent rumors in recent days about Japanese ronin and hooligans plotting to riot. The municipal authorities have repeatedly heard reports of this. On the 27th, it was repeatedly rumored that a large number of ronin and hooligans in the Yangshupu Beisichuan Road area were plotting mischief, and the concession authorities also heard about it repeatedly. Although the municipal authorities have made sufficient arrangements for public security in the city, in view of the proliferation of rumors, it is better to believe that there is a possibility than to believe that there is none. Therefore, martial law had to be implemented as a precaution. According to today's situation, it seems to have eased considerably. Regarding the rumors that the Japanese in Shanghai have already planned something, in my opinion, I believe that the Japanese authorities will not take such absurd actions. However, some ignorant ronin in Japan may be difficult to avoid overstepping the bounds, hoping to provoke major negotiations. However, the municipal authorities have paid close attention to this, and public security in the city will not be affected by unexpected events.

Receiving Commissioner: Mr. Zhang also spoke about the matter of receiving the lost territories of the Northeast. The National Government initially appointed him as the receiving commissioner. At that time, due to the severity of the situation in the city, he telegraphed requesting the appointment of other capable individuals. However, the National Government has not yet approved it. As for the receiving matters, Mr. Gu Weijun had previously convened personnel in Beiping to draft detailed rules, but due to the Japanese side's hesitation and delay, it was never realized. When Mr. Gu initially traveled south from Beiping, he telegraphed to invite me to discuss the matter. I was unable to leave Shanghai at that time, so I did not go to Nanjing.

Stabilizing Finances: Recently, the city has been affected by the current situation, with a shortage of silver and panic in the market. According to Mr. Zhang, the circulating silver in the city, to my knowledge, is about 70 million yuan, and the banknotes of all banks are about 400 million yuan. Due to the impact of the current situation, the public has saved cash, and banks have successively accumulated it, coupled with shipping it abroad to aid other ports. Therefore, panic is inevitable. The municipal authorities have discussed this matter repeatedly, and they believe that stabilizing finances starts with stabilizing public sentiment. As for banning exports, it is actually extremely difficult.

Drawing Lots Today: Mr. Zhang continued to discuss the progress of the city's business, saying that everything is proceeding as usual without any interruption. The second public land lease in the city center will be held today. Regarding the central government's fiscal austerity measures, the city will absolutely not be affected, because the city's economy, although not prosperous, is fortunately able to balance income and expenditure, so it does not feel difficult.

Ship to Japan Carrying Overseas Chinese 152

Xin Ming Wheel Set Sail Yesterday 153

Expected to Arrive in Yokohama in About Five Days 154

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was ordered by the Ministry of Communications to send the Xin Ming Wheel to Japan to carry overseas Chinese back home. Due to various procedural issues, it finally set sail for Yokohama at 6 pm yesterday. Details are as follows:

Fully Loaded with Coal and Rice: This time, the Xin Ming Wheel was ordered to go to Japan to carry overseas Chinese. Commissioner Guo Waifeng, because the overseas Chinese were unable to return home, specially prepared 100 shi of rice and a large quantity of vegetables, as well as 300 tons of tap water, as food on board. He also hired a doctor and prepared a large quantity of various medicines for medical assistance, and added a radio operator and a waiter to help the original radio operator, as well as a radio receiver and navigation instruments. Only 480 tons of coal were loaded the day before yesterday. Because the ship was still light, another 120 tons of coal were loaded in the afternoon. The Xin Ming personnel also prepared 50 shi of rice.

Xin Ming's History: The Xin Ming Wheel is the newest type of ocean-going ship in the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and has the fastest speed. It was built in 1907 and has a displacement of 2,133 tons. It was ordered to go to Kobe to load Cai Songpo's coffin and return it to China. During the Great Kanto Earthquake in Japan, it sent disaster relief rice to Yokohama. The shipowner is Ma Jiajun, the chief mate is Qian Yujia, the second mate is Zhu Shigao, and the total number of crew members is 160.

Trip to Japan: A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency met with Qian Yujia, the chief mate of the Xin Ming Wheel, yesterday to inquire about the trip to Japan. He said that Shanghai to Yokohama is 1,150 nautical miles. The Xin Ming's speed is about 12 nautical miles per hour. If there is no wind or waves, it will take about four and a half days to arrive. For example, if it sets sail at 6 pm today, it will arrive in Moji on the morning of the third day after leaving the Wusongkou and entering the East China Sea. A pilot will be hired to change the course to the Inland Sea and arrive in Bin on the morning of the fifth day. If the overseas Chinese gather in Yokohama, they can return home in Japan in one or two days.

Procedures Completed: At 10 am yesterday, Zeng Guangqing, the director of the business department of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, went to the Dalailai Steamship Company on Wuma Road to negotiate, and the Shanghai branch of the Sichuan Road Yamashita Kisen Co., Ltd. was hired as the agent for Xin Ming Yokohama. The special license was issued by the Ministry of Communications to the Jianghai Customs, and it was also issued yesterday. The customs procedures for food, coal, etc. were also completed yesterday.

Telegram to Japan: At 6 pm yesterday, the Xin Ming Wheel set sail from the Jinliyuan Pier in the French Concession. Commissioner Guo Waifeng immediately telegraphed the Ministry of Communications and the Chinese Consul in Yokohama, Mr. Zhou, to take care of the Xin Ming when it arrives in port, and to notify the overseas Chinese to prepare to avoid delays.

Banking Industry Replied to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Yesterday 157

Determined That There Will Be No Exploitation by the Enemy 158

Large-scale exports of spot silver from the city have caused extremely tight money conditions, attracting considerable attention from all walks of life. Researching the Japanese Troop Withdrawal Issue 159

Observations from the National Affairs Research Association

The Association Was Initiated by Academic Circles

Xinsheng News Agency reports: Prominent figures from academic circles in Shanghai have initiated a National Affairs Research Association, dedicated to studying foreign affairs from a national perspective. The association also aims to offer its research findings for government adoption. Such organizations are common in Europe and America, and their effectiveness is considerable. Yesterday, during its first preparatory meeting, the association briefly discussed Japan's sudden order to withdraw its troops occupying the three northeastern provinces. The consensus was that this sudden withdrawal is a delaying tactic. Japan is closely allied with France, intending to dominate Europe and America. Even strong opposition from other countries will not make Japan yield. Reports suggesting that Japan withdrew troops due to strong U.S. pressure are untrue. Japan is confident the U.S. will not declare war, allowing Soviet Russia to seize the Pacific's benefits. Japan is actively preparing to declare war on China. Therefore, Japan's troop withdrawal aims to ease international tensions, ensuring the League of Nations' resolution on the Manchurian investigation passes smoothly. Once the investigation team is appointed, Japan will use the pretext of suppressing bandits to redeploy troops. According to European telegrams, Japan's response to the League of Nations' resolution includes several proposed amendments regarding preventative measures. "Although Japan agrees to instruct commanding officers to prohibit troop advances and hostile actions, it must be stipulated that Japanese troops will retaliate if attacked by bandits." This may be part of Japan's diplomatic preparations.

Declaration of Students from Various Universities 164

Shanghai University Students' Declaration of Tears Leaving Beijing to Urge the Government to Send Troops, to All Compatriots Transmitted by National Newspapers: Since the atrocities committed by the Japanese bandits on September 18th, the government has repeatedly retreated from its duty to protect the people. Students from various universities in Shanghai, moved by righteousness, formed a team to petition in Beijing in late September. They were assured by Chairman Chiang of the National Government that the lost territories would be recovered in the shortest possible time, and that any further advance by Japanese troops would be resisted with full force. The students, believing that Chairman Chiang, as the head of state, would keep his word, returned to Shanghai and engaged in various activities to support the government. Unexpectedly, more than two months have passed, and not only have the lost territories not been recovered, but the Japanese bandits have become more rampant, and the atmosphere of aggression has intensified. Heilongjiang Province has fallen, and Tianjin and Jinzhou have been successively harassed. However, the government authorities continue to believe in the League of Nations, which has lost all hope, and there is no concrete evidence of sending troops. The students of Shanghai, heartbroken and feeling that the country will be lost soon, could no longer bear it after a long period of silence. They filled out sworn statements and freely organized a group to urge the government to send troops. Under the guidance of the Student Union, they went to Beijing again on the 24th of this month to implore the government to show a resolute determination to send troops with effective guarantees. They endured hardships along the way and finally arrived on the evening of the 25th. On the morning of the 26th, the entire group, with a spirit of extreme order and discipline, petitioned the National Government, waiting all night to see Chairman Chiang. The weather turned cold, the temperature dropped sharply, and it was snowing heavily. Faced with hunger and cold, nearly 200 students fell ill. However, all the members of the group still stood tall in the front yard, their spirits high, shouting slogans to resist Japan and save the country, their voices shaking the mountains. Students from Nanjing and some middle school students from Shanghai also arrived in support, and the number of people increased, but the order became more strict. The newspapers praised them, not to brag about our group. This time, our group was particularly strict about discipline. Before entering the National Government, all members of the group underwent several checks, and any leaflets or propaganda materials were not allowed to be carried. Due to the checking problem, some students had to return to Shanghai with pain. After entering the National Government, the group sent military police to stand guard in various places to check in and out, which was solemn and orderly, which had never happened before. The comrades believed that they would be able to gain some understanding and sympathy from the government officials. However, on the morning of the 27th, the newspapers in Beijing published a conversation with the Secretary-General of the National Government, who surprisingly said that the comrades' trip was clearly being used by others and was deliberately trying to disrupt and insult the National Government. At 2:00 PM, Chairman Chiang personally gave a speech under strict guard, beginning with harsh words accusing them of having ulterior motives, being manipulated by others, deliberately destroying, and insulting the National Government. Alas, the comrades, based on the idea that everyone is responsible for the rise and fall of the world, came to Beijing from thousands of miles away with a sincere heart to plead for the suffering compatriots in the Northeast and for the country that is in danger. They did not count the fatigue of the journey. They stood in the front yard of the National Government for two days and one night, enduring hunger, cold, and illness. The result was being slandered. At this point, the comrades did not dare to suspect that the revolutionary government would use the methods of the former warlords to suppress the patriotic movement to suppress the comrades. However, the comrades' sincere loyalty was not understood by the government. They asked themselves and were extremely sad. Fortunately, Chairman Chiang had made concrete expressions of his determination to send troops, and the Shanghai Student Union sent a telegram urging them to return. Therefore, the comrades returned to Shanghai in an orderly manner on the evening of the 28th. However, the comrades are citizens, and if the brutal bandits are not eliminated for a day, the comrades' responsibility to save the country will not be fulfilled for a day. They should stick to their original intentions and continue to struggle. The resting place is near, and they will never forget it. They also hope that the patriotic compatriots across the country will pity and teach them. This is the declaration.

Japanese in Eastern Provinces are Indirectly Spreading Propaganda

The National Christian Council of China, located at 23 Yuanmingyuan Road in Shanghai, is jointly organized by Chinese churches across the country. Reply from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce 166

Overview of Economic Severance with Japan

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, in response to a letter from the Overseas Chinese National Salvation Association of Allen Ni Lowa Province, Philippine Islands, inquiring about the domestic economic severance with Japan, replied in detail yesterday, stating: "Dear Sir, we received your letter of the 28th of this month, requesting us to show one or two aspects of the domestic anti-Japanese movement. The domestic anti-Japanese movement can be roughly divided into three categories: (1) Economic severance with Japan, the main points of which are not to import Japanese goods, not to take Japanese ships, and to sever all economic relations with the Japanese. The Japanese goods imported by various industries have been decided to be sealed up and not allowed to be sold. After the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association has accurately counted all the Japanese goods in stock, it will determine the disposal method. The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association is a joint organization of all sectors, and each industry has also established a Japanese goods inspection group, which cooperates with the Anti-Japanese Association to handle inspection matters. For goods from European and American countries shipped to China, our association has also sent letters to the Shanghai chambers of commerce of various countries, requesting them not to load Japanese ships. Since the implementation of economic severance with Japan, the Japanese shipping industry in China has been hit the hardest. Many factories set up by the Japanese in Shanghai have closed down. However, the large yarn factories are still trying their best to support, but with stockpiles of goods, they have also decided to stop production when it is unavoidable. (2) Training the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Volunteer Army. This volunteer army is organized by people from all walks of life. The chairman of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association has formed three regiments. The commercial groups that organize independently are handled by the trade associations, but they must register with the Anti-Japanese Association in order to be unified. The schools are organized by government-appointed instructors and are called the Youth Volunteer Army and do not belong to the Anti-Japanese Association. (3) Donating to the Heilongjiang military expenses. Since the invasion of the Japanese bandits, only Ma Zhanshan, the chairman of the Heilongjiang Provincial Government, has directed the resistance against the enemy, supporting it for half a month, and was trapped due to the exhaustion of food and supplies. Now he is retreating to Hailun, still planning to revive. Therefore, our association has launched a donation campaign, and all sectors have responded. The amounts remitted successively have reached hundreds of thousands. Thank you for your attention, and we hereby provide a summary for your reference."

Letter from the Ratepayers' Association to the Municipal Council 167

Patriotic Actions Should Be Understood

Undue Interference Should Not Be Applied

The Shanghai Ratepayers' Association of Chinese Nationals wrote to the Secretary-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "Dear Sir, we have received a letter from the Executive Committee of the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association stating that recently, the Shanghai Municipal Council Police have often obstructed the association's staff from performing their duties within the concession, sending them to court, etc., which has had a profound and significant impact on the future of the patriotic movement. It is important to know that since its establishment, the association has been dedicated to anti-Japanese national salvation as its purpose and is entrusted by all the citizens. Matters related to the patriotic movement, any Chinese person has a patriotic heart and would not arbitrarily destroy it. Moreover, the association's inspectors carry out their inspection duties in accordance with the association's regulations, wearing badges and staff certificates with their photos attached for identification. The inspection procedures are also carried out in accordance with the prescribed procedures and have been announced in the newspaper. Since its establishment, there have been no reports of disturbing public order. The police station, etc., have taken the above actions, which is regrettable. We hereby request your association to uphold justice and forward a letter to the Municipal Council, ordering all police stations to no longer engage in the above actions and to respect the patriotic movement." It is understood that Japan relies on its military force to invade our territory, violating international conventions and undermining world peace. The people and governments of all civilized countries recognize it as a poisonous snake and beast of humanity. Even its naval landing force relies on barbarism to land and act recklessly. Those responsible for maintaining public order tolerate it and dare not treat it with the methods used to treat our country's armed soldiers. However, the people of our country, on the one hand, must maintain the integrity of our country's sovereignty, and on the other hand, must maintain world peace, so they use non-violent methods to implement economic severance. This kind of behavior is not only a duty that the citizens should fulfill, but also indicated by Article 16 of the covenant observed by the more than fifty countries in the people's concession. It is remembered that once, the Japanese Marine Corps occupied a police station because the Public Concession detained one of its law-breaking Marine Corps members in the police station, and the matter was settled after the authorities apologized. Based on this, it can be seen that military force can destroy the law, and the authorities dare not compare with it, and instead apologize to it. However, for those who resist this kind of military force that destroys public law and invades our country's territory with non-violent economic severance to seek self-defense, undue interference is applied, and it is justified with the covenant and criminal law. This association believes that this kind of action does not sanction military force, but creates more and more military force. Those who are responsible for maintaining the law and order are only subject to the barbarism of the Japanese Marine Corps. What this association hopes from your council is that you should not fear the tyranny of military force, and you should understand the non-violent patriotic movement. In accordance with the reason in the letter, we hereby send this letter, hoping that you will investigate and handle it accordingly."

Customs Today 168

Start Collecting Disaster Relief Surtaxes

Increase on 25 Exemptions on 44

First Phase Disaster Relief Second Phase Repayment of American Wheat Principal and Interest

The collection of disaster relief surtaxes by customs offices across the country is scheduled to begin today. The Shanghai Jianghai Customs Superintendent Office has issued separate announcements to inform the public. Regarding the collection of surtaxes, the news is as follows:

Opening Process: The regulations for collecting disaster relief surtaxes and the types of goods to be taxed, after being drafted by the Ministry of Finance and submitted to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation and approval, were immediately telegraphed to customs offices throughout the country by Finance Minister Song Ziwen, preparing for the opening procedures, and ordering the collection to begin on December 1. The types of goods to be taxed were discussed in detail according to the customs tariff, with 25 types being added and 44 types being exempted.

Phased Collection: This disaster relief surtax is scheduled to be collected in two phases. The first phase will be collected at 10% of the customs tariff rate, starting from December 1 of this year to the end of July next year, for a total of seven months. During this period, all surtaxes collected will be allocated to the winter and spring relief efforts in the disaster areas of various provinces. The second phase will start on August 1, with the surtax reduced to 5%. The monthly revenue will be used to repay the principal and interest of the American wheat loan, with no fixed deadline until it is paid off. It is expected that the disaster relief surtax will be stopped after a maximum of eight months.

Sassoon Comprador Shen Yanling and 173

Divorced Concubine in Litigation

Husband and Concubine Can Break Off Relations

Mother and Son Absolutely Cannot

Shen's Concubine Sues for Return of Three Sons

Willing to Raise Them to Avoid Abuse

Cheng Yuzhen, a woman from Suzhou, is 23 years old. Eight years ago, she hung up a sign in Shanghai to work as a prostitute, named "Little Brother." In the 12th year of the Republic of China, Cheng suddenly became involved with a patron, Shen Yanling, the current comprador of the British merchant Sassoon & Co. (the son of Shanghai's famous figure Sassoon A-Si), and soon married Cheng as his concubine. After Cheng and Shen lived together, they had three sons in total: the eldest, Gongji, is currently six years old, the second, Gongwei, is four years old, and the youngest, Gongjie, is only two years old. By the autumn of this year, Cheng and Shen had disagreements. After several negotiations, they broke off their relationship and made a contract. Article 2 of the contract stated that Cheng's maternal status and all legal rights to her three biological sons were forever forfeited. Afterwards, Cheng hired two lawyers, Zhu Sifu and Jiang Yiping, to sue Shen in the First Special Court, requesting that Article 2 of the contract be declared invalid. The reason was that Shen knew that Cheng Yuzhen had lost her education at a young age and did not understand literature, and that he had not obtained Cheng's consent, nor had he invited Yuzhen's agent lawyer Zhu Sifu to the scene to testify, so Article 2 of the contract could not be valid. After the trial judge Yang Yi ruled that "the agreement between the two parties to separate was confirmed, and the part of Article 2 concerning the loss of the plaintiff's maternal status and all legal rights to Gongji, Gongwei, and Gongjie was invalid." The reasons for the ruling were that the combination of the plaintiff and the defendant could be dissolved by contract, but the relationship between mother and son was a natural combination, not created by contract, nor could it be eliminated by contract. Moreover, there was no reason for a son to sever relations with his mother, and their maternal status could not be eliminated due to the separation of the family. As for all legal rights between mother and son due to the maternal relationship, they would naturally follow their identity and could not be deprived. Moreover, the plaintiff's relationship with her three sons was not something that the defendant could freely dispose of. The defendant, based solely on his own or his concubine's intentions, completely disposed of the plaintiff's maternal relationship, which was directly using the status of a third party as the object of their disposal, which was not in accordance with the law or human sentiment. This kind of contract violated good morals and could hardly be considered valid. Since this case was ruled in favor of Cheng Yuzhen, Cheng still hired lawyers Zhu Sifu and Jiang Yiping to file a suit with the Mediation Office of the First Special Court, suing Shen and requesting mediation, ordering Shen to hand over the three thousand to the petitioner Cheng Yuzhen for self-support. The petition stated that Article 2 of the contract signed by the petitioner and Shen had been declared invalid by the court. Now it has been found that Shen and his wife have angered the sons born to her because they have not won the lawsuit with the petitioner, and often abuse them. His wife, who still has the ability to bear children, is determined to put Gongji and others to death. The petitioner is still alive, how can she sit idly by and watch her own children being bullied? Moreover, the relationship between mother and son is rooted in nature, and there is no reason to not save them in times of danger. For this reason, she has no choice but to petition the court to summon her case for mediation, ordering the respondent to hand over Gongji, Gongwei, and Gongjie, who were born to the petitioner, to the petitioner for self-support. The case concerns the lives of four mothers and sons, and she begs that you summon her for inquiry soon. The court, based on the statement, summoned the mediation in the ninth court by judge Li Mo yesterday morning. However, Shen Yanling did not appear as summoned. Judge Li then declared that there was no way to mediate, and informed the plaintiff's lawyer Li that if the respondent Shen Yanling did not report to the court within five days, it should be considered that the mediation had failed and that a formal lawsuit could be filed separately.

Renting a House Must Add Insurance 174

The First Special District Court of Jiangsu Shanghai replied to the Shanghai Real Estate Association, stating: "Dear Sir, we have received your letter regarding the request for instructions from Xielong Company on the matter of adding insurance for tenants renting houses. If it is stipulated by laws and regulations that renting a house must add insurance, both the landlord and the tenant should comply with it. However, this matter originally belonged to the procedures that the parties to the contract should have at the beginning of the lease. If the tenant does not agree to add insurance, the landlord should not be allowed to refuse the lease. If the lease contract has already been established, and it is considered that the tenant still needs to add insurance at this time, the landlord should directly negotiate with the tenant to handle it. We approve of the letter before, and we should reply accordingly, hoping for your reference."

Su Yingjie 178

Sued by Concubine for Neglecting Support

Su Yingjie, the principal of the Nanshi Municipal Middle School, and his concubine Gu Shanbao, had separated last year due to differences in opinion, with lawyers providing proof. It is said that the issue of money has not been settled. In June of this year, Su Gu Shanbao filed a petition to the mediation office of the local court, requesting alimony, but the proceedings were not resolved because Su Yingjie did not appear. Gu Shanbao has now hired lawyers Jin Yu and Liu Shiqi to file a lawsuit in the local court on behalf of her 12-year-old son Su Zuliang, with Shanbao as the legal guardian, accusing Su Yingjie of abandonment and neglect of support. The objectives are: (1) Defendant Su Yingjie should pay a lump sum of 6,000 yuan in alimony. (2) Defendant should pay 600 yuan for Zuliang's three years of tuition and 1,180 yuan for three years of living expenses. The statement roughly stated that after plaintiff Shanbao met the defendant in the eighth year of the Republic, they fell in love and lived together, and subsequently had a son named Zuliang. Later, the defendant's wife died, and she took over the household. Unexpectedly, the defendant later took in another concubine, leading to constant disputes and unrest. The later concubine was young and beautiful, and engaged in contention for affection, and constantly slandered her. The plaintiff was not good at flattery, and was preoccupied with household affairs, and appeared more haggard. The defendant found the plaintiff old and undesirable, and abandoned her like a worn-out shoe, only allowing the plaintiff to live with her mother because she had borne a son. Before the plaintiff returned to her mother's house, the defendant promised to pay 50 yuan per month for alimony, and the defendant would also pay for the clothing and tuition fees for the plaintiff and her son. The plaintiff hoped that he would change his mind, so she obeyed and left. Unexpectedly, the defendant only paid the alimony in full for the first few months, and then stopped paying the checks, and procrastinated when she asked for payment, and this has been going on for four years. The livelihood of the mother and son has been maintained entirely by the plaintiff. The defendant has not asked about it, and they are like strangers. Last year, she entrusted lawyer Chao Kun to recover the principal and interest of the deposit from the defendant, but the defendant ignored it, and she had no choice but to file a lawsuit. The defendant Su Yingjie also hired lawyer Jiang Baolian to defend him. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang Run specially opened the eighth court to hear the case. Both parties were absent, and only the lawyers appeared in court. First, the plaintiff's lawyer stated the plaintiff's age, roughly stating that the plaintiff Su Gu Shanbao was 31 years old and from Suzhou, and stated the previous events. He also said that the elder son of the first wife, Zu Hua, also recognized the plaintiff as his stepmother, and that Zuliang was studying in Suzhou, and the defendant also came forward. Next, the defendant's lawyer stated that the defendant Su Yingjie was 58 years old, from Shanghai, and lived in a private school. The plaintiff was not recognized as the first wife, and the son Zuliang was indeed born to the plaintiff, but previously, lawyer Chao Kun had mediated a settlement, and they had separated. The judge stated that both parties must be present in person for the case to be reviewed, and adjourned the court.

Zhang Weiliang and Wife Reconcile

Reconciliation Terms Agreed Upon in Court

Zhang Weiliang, a dentist at No. 9 Hankou Road, Jiangxi Road, met Dong Meizhen, a top student from the Patriotic Girls' School, in the twelfth year of the Republic. At that time, Dong was only twenty-three years old and unmarried, while Zhang was three years older and also single. A woman waiting for marriage is easily tempted by a gentleman. They began with friendly interactions and after a year, they found each other very affectionate. Dong then requested a formal marriage to establish their status, but Zhang refused a ceremony, saying that his family was old-fashioned and his mother did not approve of free love. They lived together without a matchmaker. Later, Zhang's mother knew about it and did not object. Seven years have passed, and their love gradually faded. Zhang's mother was still unhappy that this daughter-in-law had not been formally married and often told her son that she would find another good wife for him, which made Zhang unable to devote himself to Dong. Last year, Dong's niece came to live with the Zhang family, and Zhang was envious of her youth and beauty and wanted to take advantage of her. However, Dong was watching closely, and he could not get started. Recently, when the girl got married, Dong had to send a gift, but Zhang was jealous and refused to give anything. Then Dong and Zhang had a conflict, and Zhang's mother took the opportunity to stir up trouble, so Zhang's determination to remarry became stronger. Dong learned that the wedding date had been set and feared that once it was realized, she would be abandoned. She hired a lawyer to petition the First Special District Local Court, requesting mediation to prevent Zhang from remarrying and to continue living together. Yesterday morning, Presiding Judge Zhou Daren specially opened a mediation court. Both parties were present. Many of Dong's classmates were in the audience, and the eighth courtroom was filled with women. Judge Zhou first asked Dong Meizhen about the course of their relationship and the origins of the current conflict, then asked Zhang Weiliang what the nature of his cohabitation with Dong was. Zhang said that it was from friendship to marriage, and if he wanted to continue living together, she had to be respectful to his mother and listen to his commands. Dong expressed complete acceptance of the two points Zhang said. Judge Zhou then drafted the reconciliation terms: Zhang Weiliang was willing to continue living with Dong Meizhen as husband and wife and would not remarry. Dong Meizhen was willing to obey Zhang Weiliang's reasonable commands and get along with Zhang Weiliang's mother, otherwise, they would resolve it according to law and remarry. Both parties expressed satisfaction and signed successively, and then reconciled.

Tang Min Accuses 179

Shen Zuwang of Fraudulent Marriage and Abuse

Requests 30,000 Yuan in Alimony

Tang Min (aka Muying), a Zhejiang woman with higher education, recently hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the First Special Court against Shen Zuwang for fraudulent marriage, abuse, and theft of dowry, requesting a divorce, the return of the dowry, compensation for damages, and 30,000 yuan in alimony. It is reported that the case will be heard in the civil court on the 2nd of this month. The general idea of her statement is that in August of last year, the defendant entrusted Ms. Deng Baozhen to propose marriage, saying that his first wife had died, that he was extremely honest, had no vices, and worked at the Shanghai Securities and Goods Exchange, and that they were well-matched. The plaintiff believed this to be true and agreed to the marriage. They married in October. Unexpectedly, after the defendant saw that his scheme had succeeded, he pursued his original intention of stealing the dowry. He used various means to forcibly take away the plaintiff's various ornaments such as pearl hairpins, necklaces, beads, emeralds, diamonds, etc. In February of this year, when the plaintiff went to Hangzhou to visit her relatives, he secretly opened the plaintiff's suitcase, and when the plaintiff returned to Shanghai, she realized that the jewelry and other ornaments stored in the suitcase were gone. When she asked him for it, she was beaten by his mother, and he colluded with his unmarried sister, Shen Lingwan, to abuse her together, constantly scolding and beating her, which led to chronic illness. The defendant also constantly provoked fights and beatings. She was already sick in bed, but could not withstand the beating, which caused her to cough up blood and become unconscious, her life in danger. The defendant saw that the ornaments had been stolen and treated the plaintiff inhumanely. Recently, it was learned that he was wandering outside day and night, smoking opium, and had no legitimate occupation. His first wife, Ms. Yuan Cuifang, is still alive. She divorced last time due to abuse and did not die of illness. This shows the darkness of his family and the maliciousness of his intentions.

Yong'an Savings Department 180

Employee Accused of Embezzling Funds

Sentenced to One Year in Prison and Fined 500 Yuan

Chao Kuixiang, a native of Changzhou who was an employee in the Hongkou branch of the Yong'an Savings Department at No. 501 North Sichuan Road, was found by accountant Wang Jiguang to have discrepancies in his accounts from September of the year before last to last year. When asked, Chao admitted to temporarily using the money and promised to repay it in installments. As a result, his monthly salary of 40 yuan was deducted, and the matter was not pursued. Unexpectedly, he was unable to make up the shortfall, and avoided going to the bank to work for about three weeks. The Hongkou police were informed and sent detective Feng Qi to find him at No. 20 Yongshou Cemetery on Fangbang Road in the Chinese district the day before yesterday. He was brought to the police station. He admitted that most of the embezzled funds, totaling 8,400 yuan, were deposited in the Yuankang Qianzhuang on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession, but the bank had already closed. Yesterday morning, the police sent Chao to the First Special Court's Criminal Division. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that the plaintiff had already filed a lawsuit against Yuankang Zhuang in the First Special Court of the French Concession. The defendant, the police, admitted to embezzling a total of 11,000 yuan and returning more than 1,000 yuan. The plaintiff's incidental civil suit must wait until the Second Special District's lawsuit is over before it can be concluded. Wang Jiguang, the representative of the plaintiff, Yong'an Savings Department, stated the previous events and presented the accounts for inspection through a lawyer. When questioned, the defendant confessed that he had been confused for a moment and had been fooled by others. Judge Xiao Xie□ reviewed the confession and sentenced Chao Kuixiang to one year in prison and fined him 500 yuan. If the fine is converted into imprisonment, it will be calculated at two yuan per day. The incidental civil suit was transferred to the Civil Division of this court for trial. The defendant also has a civil lawsuit in the Second Special Court, which is scheduled to be heard on the afternoon of December 4. The police are allowed to send detectives to send the defendant for questioning.

Ban on Small Temple Names Wearing Boy Scout Uniforms 181

The Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau issued Public Notice Zheng No. 26 yesterday, stating, "Received Municipal Government Order No. 10428, approving the Chinese Boy Scout Headquarters Letter No. 6346, according to the Shanghai Boy Scout Council report stating that recently in Shanghai, numerous bands and small temple names have been found employing ignorant young children, wearing Boy Scout uniforms, to perform funeral and wedding services, obscuring society, and that while this behavior does not merit the notice of those in the know, it has a bearing on the future development of the Boy Scouts. Therefore, the board of directors decided at the second regular meeting to request that the headquarters issue a clear order to ban this activity, for the sake of the public. Accordingly, we respectfully submit this document to your department, hoping that you will examine it, quickly ban this activity, and serve the public interest. Based on this, we find that Boy Scout uniforms are of great importance. If ignorant people are allowed to imitate and wear them at will, it will not only hinder the uniformity of Boy Scout uniforms, but also cause incidents and damage the reputation of the Boy Scouts. We should write to your municipal government, ordering your subordinates to strictly ban this activity to protect the development of the local Boy Scout movement, for the sake of the Party. We have approved this, and in addition to sending a letter in reply, we should order the bureau to immediately comply with it, ordering the subordinates to strictly ban this activity. This notice is hereby issued. You must comply with it within one month. If you delay deliberately, you will be severely punished."

China Travel Service Establishes Wuhu Branch 182

A Branch Opened in Baxianqiao

Both Scheduled to Open Today

The China Travel Service at No. 114 Sichuan Road in this city has always aimed to serve the public and facilitate travel. In addition to opening branches in major commercial ports in the country, it has recently decided that Wuhu is an important port on the Yangtze River and that it is necessary to add a branch. It has specially dispatched staff to prepare for it. After a month, a branch has been opened in the Shanghai Bank on Jinbao Street in Wuhu, scheduled to open on December 1. It will sell tickets for various Yangtze River ships without charging a handling fee and will have uniformed attendants at the pier to take care of everything. The company, considering the vast area of this city, has also opened a branch in the Shanghai Bank in Baxianqiao, in addition to setting up a branch in Jing'an Temple Road in West Shanghai and an office in Hongkou, to facilitate travel for residents of the French Concession. It will also sell tickets for various vehicles and ships, also scheduled to open today (December 1).

Candle Industry Petitions for Correction of Stamp Tax on Gift Certificates 183

The Shanghai Candle Industry Association, on behalf of its member Mao Yuyuan Company, whose twelve gift certificates (candle tickets) were seized by the stamp tax inspector, and the Public Security Bureau immediately imposed a heavy fine, believes that this action violates the regulations promulgated by the Ministry. The association sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting that it be forwarded to the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau for correction in accordance with the law, in order to eliminate malpractices and avoid disputes. The original text is recorded as follows: "Presented for the purpose of requesting the Shangbao Stamp Tax Branch to correct the illegal seizure of gift certificates issued by commercial firms, and the dispatch of the same to the Public Security Bureau for punishment, in order to prevent future malpractices and disputes. It is reported that the association's inspectors took twelve gift certificates (candle tickets) and immediately dispatched them to the First District Office of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, which ordered a fine of 30 yuan to be paid within three days, an erroneous measure. We request that the matter be forwarded for relief. Since the incident occurred, the members have been panicked and continue to appeal to the association, believing that the candle tickets issued by candle shops are like the gift certificates issued by banks and companies. For example, if a customer buys a catty of candles, they first pay for a catty of candles, then the shop fills out a ticket, affixes a stamp according to the amount, and hands it over to the customer. When the customer needs candles, they bring the candle ticket to the shop to exchange for candles. This candle ticket is actually the same as the goods. Now the branch believes that the candle ticket is not affixed with a stamp and considers it a violation of the stamp tax regulations. It is as if when merchants sell goods, they must not only affix stamps to the invoice, but also affix a stamp to each item. The issuance of species tax tickets (for soda and foreign wine). However, the candle industry is not included. Now the branch distorts the Ministry's documents, imposes fines on merchants at will, and if this bad precedent is set, it will not only harm the industry but also disrupt commerce. The most team-oriented organization should be asked to open a petition to the Shanghai Municipal Commerce Transport Institute, find a way to correct it, and for this, we request the Qian Council to quickly forward it to the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau, ordering the branch to immediately correct it to eliminate malpractices and avoid disputes. This is truly for the public good."

Songhu Train Injures a Horse 184

At about 2 PM yesterday, a soldier from the Tax Police Regiment of the Ministry of Finance stationed in Songhu was riding a horse on duty when he passed by the Songhu Railway tracks west of Songxing Road in Wusong. As the Songhu train approached, the driver sounded the horn as a warning. To avoid danger, the soldier quickly dismounted. Unexpectedly, the horse was startled by the sound of the horn and ran onto the tracks, where it was hit by the train and had its hind legs crushed. Fortunately, no one was injured. The soldier returned to camp and reported to his superior, who gathered many soldiers to carry the injured horse away.

Women's National Salvation Grand Alliance 186

Your common hatred of the enemy and heartfelt words are deeply admired. However, it is an overestimation to worry about the lack of consolation funds. Who does not like doing good deeds as much as I do? In a storm and a dangerous boat, our souls and bodies should all be dedicated to the country, especially when everyone is working together, and there are ladies like you responding from high places. The colleagues here are organizing a group to comfort the soldiers who are protecting the country and are hereby informed. I hope that everyone will work together with one heart and one mind to overcome the difficulties of the times. The Women's National Salvation Grand Alliance respectfully bows.

Domestic Newspapers Request Tax Exemption 189

Domestic newspapers manufactured by Tianzhang Paper Mill and others are purchased in large quantities in Fujian and Xiamen, but the tax burden is inevitably heavier. The Fujian Provincial Association for the Promotion of Domestic Goods has petitioned the Ministry of Finance to approve the exemption of domestic newspapers from all taxes to show support. The petition reads: "For the matter of petitioning, the paper required by various newspapers in our country has always been taken from foreign goods. The leakage is huge and shocking. I have found that the Shanghai factory already has domestic products that are excellent, suitable, and no less than imported goods. However, our domestic products have been subject to customs restrictions for many years, resulting in heavy costs and difficulty in promotion. If we do not urgently seek to save them, it will be difficult for domestic goods to compete with foreign goods. The way to save them lies in the government's practical assistance and special awards, so that domestic products can make great progress and benefit both the national economy and people's livelihood. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce, together with the three ministries of Railways, Communications, and Finance, presented and approved by the Executive Yuan in the 19th year of the Republic of China, listed the machine-made paper industry in Article 2 of the Provisional Standards for Examination of Special Industrial Awards, and in Article 5, it stated that according to the provisions of Article 2 of this Law, materials may be subject to reduced transportation costs or tax exemptions, all limited to domestic goods, but important materials without domestic production may also be subject to appropriate reductions and exemptions. Then, the aforementioned domestic newspapers are machine-made and completely domestic goods. The Department should approve the tax exemption, in order to show excellence. The association, in order to promote the promotion of domestic goods and save the country, should prepare a document for inspection and verification. Please implement it, and please instruct and comply."

Songhu Train Crushes a Horse 190

At around 2 PM yesterday afternoon, a soldier from the Tax Police Corps of the Ministry of Finance stationed in Songhu was riding a horse on duty when he was traveling west on Songxing Road in Wusong, next to the Songhu Railway tracks. When the Songhu train arrived at that location, the driver saw the situation and sounded the horn as a warning. To avoid danger, the soldier quickly dismounted, but the horse, hearing the sound of the horn, was startled and ran onto the tracks, where it was hit by the train and its hind legs were crushed. Fortunately, no one was injured. The soldier returned to camp and reported to his officer, who gathered many soldiers to carry the injured horse away.
