Special Shipping News 196

Collision of Two Ships: The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Jiahe" vessel, en route from Shanghai to Yingkou to load cargo, dropped anchor upon arrival in Yingkou port. Due to tidal wave surges, the Jiahe's anchor chain dragged behind the ship. Coincidentally, the company's "Taishun" vessel also arrived in Yingkou, attempting to cross the channel, and struck the Jiahe's anchor chain. The Taishun's bow then violently collided with the Jiahe's port side, causing a large hole above the waterline, measuring one foot above and seven feet wide between the seams. The second-deck platform was also destroyed. The Taishun repeatedly collided three times, causing the Jiahe to run aground after the damage. Subsequent investigation revealed extensive losses. The Jiahe's owner telegraphed Shanghai to report the incident and requested the Yingkou branch to prepare materials for repairing the breach. A warning was also issued to all vessels entering Yingkou port to avoid the Jiahe's grounded location. The ship is currently undergoing salvage efforts.

Shanghai-Tianjin Shipping: Following the Tianjin Incident, various shipping companies in Shanghai received telegrams from Tianjin stating that it was extremely dangerous for merchant ships to load and unload cargo in Tianjin. Consequently, all cargo transport from Shanghai to Tianjin was suspended. As of yesterday, the shipping companies received further telegrams from Tianjin indicating that while the crisis in Tianjin had not completely subsided, the situation had slightly improved. Chinese ships arriving in Tianjin mostly unloaded cargo at Tanggu. Those entering the port berthed along the Bund within the British concession, ensuring the safety of passengers. However, all passenger services have been suspended, and no goods are being exported from Tianjin. Currently, only one Chinese merchant ship is operating between Shanghai and Tianjin.

Public Safety Bureau Implements Winter Defense 197

The Municipal Public Safety Bureau customarily designates December 1st of each year to the end of February of the following year as the "Winter Defense Period." As the Winter Defense Period has arrived today, Director Chen has instructed all district offices to implement Winter Defense as per usual, intensifying patrols, reducing training hours, and increasing patrol shifts. Due to the recent proliferation of rumors in Shanghai, the bureau had already implemented patrol measures similar to those of the Winter Defense Period several days ago. However, starting today, greater emphasis will be placed on defensive measures.

Chen Xizeng, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Safety Bureau, announced that the November police salaries for all district office and team leaders under his jurisdiction had been received from the Municipal Finance Bureau. He instructed the respective district office and team leaders to collect the salaries from the bureau yesterday and distribute them to their respective officers for their use.

Record of the Fourth Preparatory Meeting of the Municipal Farmers' Association 201

The Preparatory Committee of the Farmers' Association held its fourth preparatory meeting at the meeting hall in Fuyuan Lane, Xizang Road, yesterday at 4:00 PM. Fifteen committee members attended, with Zhang Huinian serving as chairman and Lu Shuyang as recorder. After the chairman reported on recent preparatory work, discussions were held. Agenda items: (1) Amending the draft constitution of the association. Resolution: Amended and passed. (2) Committee member Chen Ya-fu requested to resign from his concurrent position as Standing Committee member. Resolution: Unanimously retained. (3) Committee member Chen Ya-fu proposed that due to the continuous rain this year, the city's crops have suffered greatly, and a good harvest is hopeless. As winter approaches, farmers will inevitably lack food and clothing. Therefore, it is requested that the authorities be urged to promptly devise a relief plan. Resolution: Request the Social Affairs Bureau to establish farmers' loan funds and price stabilization measures, and to distribute winter clothing for relief. (4) Committee member Yu Zhenhui proposed that the association issue a circular regarding the current situation, calling for peaceful reunification and joint efforts to overcome the national crisis. Resolution: Passed. To be drafted and issued by the Standing Committee. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM, followed by a dinner. During the dinner, opinions were exchanged regarding association affairs, and detailed plans were discussed.

Japanese Warship "Muroto" Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 202

Docked at Osaka Wharf, Carrying Hundreds of Marines

The Japanese warship "Muroto" arrived at Wusong on the 29th of this month and entered the Huangpu River yesterday, currently docked at the Osaka Wharf. Marines from the ship went ashore yesterday, but only patrolled within the foreign concessions and did not enter the Chinese areas.

Municipal Government Investigates Unemployment Figures 203

The Municipal Government instructed the Social Affairs Bureau in response to a communication from the Ministry of Interior Affairs, stating that due to the economic downturn in recent years, the cost of living has become increasingly difficult, and the panic of unemployment has spread throughout the country. If relief is not urgently sought, starvation and cold will lead to desperate measures, posing a significant threat to social order. Recognizing this, the Ministry has specially designed a survey form to investigate the number of unemployed and jobless individuals within the country. The aim is to first understand the general situation to facilitate unified relief efforts. In addition to issuing instructions to various provincial governments and civil affairs departments, the survey form is enclosed for your city government's reference. You are instructed to have your subordinates fill it out according to the form and submit it to the Ministry within two months for statistical purposes. The survey form is divided into seven categories: agriculture, industry, mining, commerce, military/police, civil servants, and freelancers. Additionally, individuals aged 16 to 40 are categorized separately from those aged 41 to 60, further differentiating by gender, for verification purposes.

Shanghai-Manzhouli Airmail Temporarily Suspended 204

According to a Shanghai Post Office announcement, airmail services via the Shanghai-Manzhouli route are temporarily suspended due to the complete suspension of flights along the line. All airmail transiting through this route has been temporarily suspended for acceptance.

Bank of China Inspection Report 205

Forty-Fifth Inspection

The forty-fifth inspection report of the Shanghai Bank of China Issuance Reserve Inspection Committee states that the committee members, along with entrusted accountants, conducted the forty-fifth inspection of the Shanghai Bank of China's headquarters' and its affiliated banks' issuance and exchange coupon reserve vault on November 29, 1931, in accordance with the committee's rules. The Director of the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance also joined the inspection. The results of the inspection are listed below: Total amount of exchange coupon issuance: 127,799,932 yuan, including 66,159,052 yuan issued by the headquarters, 31,544,056 yuan used by affiliated banks, and 30,096,824 yuan used by various banks and firms. Excluding the portion used by various banks and firms, which will be inspected separately according to the original method, this inspection covers the portion used by the headquarters and affiliated banks as follows: Amount issued by the headquarters and used by affiliated banks: 97,700,3108 yuan. Amount of reserve for exchange coupons of the headquarters and affiliated banks: 97,700,3108 yuan, including cash reserve of 58,734,822.98 yuan and guarantee reserve of 38,968,285.02 yuan. The above two items, totaling 60% in cash reserve and 40% in guarantee reserve, have been verified to be correct in amount. In accordance with Article 5 of the rules, this formal report is issued on November 29, 1931, by Xu Kan, Director of the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance, Pei Yunqing and Wang Yansong, representatives of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, Hu Mengjia and Wu Yunzhai, representatives of the Shanghai Banking Association, Li Jisheng and Yan Junan, representatives of the Shanghai Money Exchange Association, Yan Xifan and Xia Guichu, representatives of coupon-issuing banks and firms, and Zhou Zongliang, Ye Zhuotang, Li Zhilian, and Xu Ji□, representatives of the directors and supervisors of the Bank of China, and accountant Yu Zikang.

Three Kidnappers on Guangzhou Steamer 206

Relief association investigators Chen Shaoting and Lin Yongfang, along with water police detectives Wu Wenqing and others, apprehended three kidnappers, Dong Jinsheng, Fan Ganchen, and Wang Shouliu, and rescued four kidnapped children, Guo Jiaqing, Jiao Jinsheng, Zhang Arong, and Lei Laifa, on the Guangzhou steamer bound for Xiamen at the Swire Company wharf yesterday. The kidnappers intended to sell the children in Xiamen. Due to differences in accent, detectives questioned them and discovered that the gang was organized. The children had been kidnapped for half a month and were initially locked in a room on the third floor, where they were threatened and forced to call the kidnappers "father." They were then taken to the port for export. The kidnappers have been detained at the water police station and transferred to the local court for interrogation.

Robbery at Nanyang Bridge 207

A Pistol Also Stolen

At Xu Guoguang's residence at No. 10 Quanyunan, Nanyang Bridge, outside the West Gate, six robbers suddenly appeared at 9:30 AM yesterday. One was wearing a gabardine coat, one a black coat, and four were wearing short coats. They were armed with two pistols and one Mauser pistol. Xu was not at home at the time. The robbers entered the house, tied up Xu's family members, and ransacked the boxes and chests, stealing only a few pieces of clothing. However, they also stole Xu's pistol, serial number 44921 (registered with the French police). Upon returning home and freeing his family, Xu reported the robbery to the relevant police station and other police stations, requesting investigation and apprehension.

Six robbers, one armed with a pistol, broke into No. 243 Yuezhou Road, Hudong, at around 4:20 PM yesterday. They threatened the victim, preventing them from making any noise, and searched the premises intently. However, they found no valuables, leaving them disappointed.

Several articles of clothing were stolen. The victim reported the incident to the police station, requesting apprehension of the robbers.

Face Friend Sales are Thriving 210

Misleading Rumors that Anti-Japanese Association Has Certified it as Non-Japanese Goods

"Face Friend," managed by Baichang Company at No. 96 Beijing Road, Shanghai, is selling very well. The reason for its popularity is undoubtedly its high quality and lack of oil. Therefore, women from all walks of life are happy to purchase it. Because no other products need to be used after application, regular use can make the skin fair and white, eliminate freckles, minimize pores, and prevent aging. Applying it every morning can keep the skin clean and white all day long. It is now heard that the company, in order to satisfy customers, has recently increased the volume compared to before, while maintaining the same price. It has also been learned that the product has been approved and registered by the Trademark Bureau of the Ministry of Industry of the National Government and has received a certificate from the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, proving that it is definitely not Japanese goods. Therefore, the number of buyers has increased even more recently.

Confucian Doctor Jin Jinshan Comes to Shanghai to Practice Medicine 211

Jin Jinshan, a renowned doctor from northern Anhui and grandson of the famous official and Qing Urumqi Viceroy Jin Gong, eschewed fame and focused on medicine from a young age. His reputation is highly regarded in the Huai River region, and those seeking medical treatment come from far and wide. Dr. Jin has saved many lives. Last year, he was hired by the Fufeng Yutong Western Flour Company to serve as a medical and pharmaceutical consultant in Shanghai. Wishing to use his medical skills to benefit the world, Dr. Jin now practices medicine in Ruizhi Lane, Wuding Road, in the International Settlement. Recently, many have sought his treatment, drawn by his reputation.

Change of Leadership at National News Agency 212

The Shanghai National News Agency has been established for eight years. It was initially the Shanghai propaganda arm of the Kuomintang Central Party Headquarters, with Shao Ji'ang as its director. In the winter of 1926, He Weixin took over. After the April 1927 purge, the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters sent Zhang Jinglu to take over, with Chen Dezheng serving as director. In the summer of 1929, Chen resigned, and Tang Demin succeeded him. Tang has achieved significant results in the past three years. Recently, Tang 君 is starting a new China News Agency and is unable to continue in his current role. The Municipal Party Headquarters has appointed Du Gang as his replacement. Du is scheduled to take office today and will move the agency's address to the Shengsheng Silk Shop in Qinghe Lane, Zhoujin Lane, Simalu (Fourth Avenue). Du is interested in the news business and will actively develop the agency's affairs in the future. It is also heard that Tang Demin's newly established China News Agency will be located at the old address of the National News Agency at No. 130 Jiaotong Road, Qipan Street.

Lianyi Charity Association Plans Winter Relief 213

The Shanghai Lianyi Charity Association's headquarters, located on the second floor at Xiangfen Lane entrance, Nanjing Road, has historically distributed winter relief. Considering the severe flooding in various regions this year and the large number of refugees seeking shelter in Shanghai, providing winter relief is especially urgent. In light of this, association directors Xu Qianlin, Yuan Ludeng, Zhu Yinjiang, and Lu Wenzhong have initiated preparations. However, the association's finances are already strained. Since this matter is of great importance, it is difficult to achieve widespread effectiveness without soliciting donations from all sectors of society. The charitable individuals in all sectors will surely be willing to help. The association's donation collection points are at the Women's Commercial Savings Bank on Nanjing Road and the Yitai Company in Shanshou Lane, Broadway Road, Hongkou. Donors can directly send donations to the above locations, where official donation receipts will be issued for verification.

Lunyuan Silk Shop's Carelessness 214

The Lunyuan Silk Shop at No. 1 Shuiqing Lane, Ningbo Road, experienced a fire on the morning of the 28th of last month at 2:00 AM due to carelessness. The fire lasted for half an hour. The fire and water damage are estimated to be over 100,000 yuan, with water damage accounting for the majority. The goods are valuable silks and satins ordered from factories in France, Germany, and Switzerland, featuring novel designs and no Japanese goods whatsoever. Fortunately, the goods worth over 30,000 yuan stored upstairs were spared. The losses have been insured against fire. The manager and shareholders of the shop are reputable and trustworthy merchants.

Problem of Printing Materials for Tobacco Factories 217

Letter from Chairman of Tobacco Factories Association to Chairman of Colored Printing Industry Association: Greetings. Our member companies, Huacheng and Huada Tobacco Companies, experienced delays in the distribution of tobacco products to Guangdong due to the mistaken identification of the goods as Japanese. We are very grateful for your association's telegram certifying that the goods are entirely domestic. Subsequently, we received your letter requesting that our association instruct Huacheng and Huada to entrust their printing permanently to your association. We have already conveyed this to the two companies. Since the economic severance with Japan, our colleagues in the industry have never lagged behind in their patriotic spirit. On September 29th, we gathered representatives from various industry associations to conduct a thorough discussion and seek a complete solution. Later, I personally attended your association's meeting and proposed that all printing used by our member tobacco factories be entrusted to your association, but this was not adopted. After certifying the Guangdong-bound tobacco products of Huacheng and Huada, you claimed to bear considerable responsibility and requested permanent printing, refusing to accept all printing and addressing the issue piecemeal, which is difficult to understand. I have scheduled a meeting for 6:30 PM on December 2nd, inviting your association members, including Mr. Lu Fengzhu, Wang Jinshi, Huang Zhongming, and Hu Peiran, to discuss a fundamental solution in order to achieve universality and openness. Please be informed accordingly.

The Tragic History of the Fall of Korea to be Published 218

The Anti-Japanese Propaganda Department has collected "Notes to Inspire Hatred Against Japan" and "The Bloody History of the Korean Independence Movement" and other books, compiling them into a book titled "The Tragic History of the Fall of Korea." The entire book is approximately 100,000 words, in a finely bound pocket-sized format for easy carrying. The book has been finalized and will soon be sent to print. Please Maintain the Original Name of the Physicians' Association 220

The National Physicians' Association submitted a petition to the Central Training Department and the Department of Health, requesting the retention of the original name of the Physicians' Association in order to ensure consistency in governance and naming. The association stated that it had recently received letters from the Physicians' Associations of Wuxian and Kunming City, stating that they had received instructions from the Party Affairs Consolidation Committee of the county and the Party Affairs Guidance Committee of the city, respectively, stating that, according to instructions from the Central Training Department, they were to rename the Wuxian Physicians' Association as the Wuxian Western Medicine Association and the Kunming City Physicians' Association as the Kunming City Western Medicine Physicians' Association, etc. Upon receiving these letters, the association asked whether the nomenclature across the country was to be unified and whether the renaming of the association was appropriate. The association deliberated in detail at its tenth executive committee meeting, believing that academics should not be limited by national borders, and medicine should treat all equally. Under the current party governance, consolidation, and construction, everything is being renewed. The so-called "new" largely adopts the practices of advanced countries, aiming for progress, without being slave to Chinese/foreign, North/South, East/West distinctions. Looking back at our four thousand years of craftsmanship, arts, culture, clothing, and customs, we have almost always possessed the ability to be pioneers and visionaries. However, times have changed, and today we find ourselves constantly lagging behind. Consequently, in the past century, the influence of Western culture has swept eastward, unstoppable. Today, what the country values is Western methods, what it learns is Western methods, what it implements is Western methods, and what it uses is Western things. The government leads from above, and the people follow from below. Patriotic individuals cannot help but feel ashamed that China's sages do not arise, and we are increasingly becoming barbarians. However, under these circumstances, in order to defend ourselves and survive, we have no choice but to abandon our weaknesses and adopt others' strengths. Therefore, the Westernization of techniques in the country today is not limited to medicine alone. There is no reason for medicine to be uniquely different simply because it is Western. Moreover, although the term "physician" is not an ancient one, it has been in use for almost thirty years. The informed almost universally recognize it as the name for scientific medicine. Society is accustomed to it, uses it in writing, and the medical community accepts it. It is expected that scientific medicine will advance and flourish with the progress of the nation, spreading throughout the land of Yu and Shenzhou (China), becoming as common as the transformation of caterpillars, and standing alongside lawyers, pharmacists, accountants, engineers, architects, and other professionals, working together in the international community, unifying their names, unifying their realities, and not differentiating themselves simply because their knowledge comes from the West. There is also no reason for medicine to be uniquely different simply because it is Western. Furthermore, according to the instructions of the Party Departments of Wuxian and Kunming City, they are either to be renamed as Western Medicine Associations or Western Medicine Physicians' Associations. Regarding the term "physician," it seems to be discarded and rejected like worn-out shoes. Investigation reveals that the establishment of Physicians' Associations is not limited to these few locations across the country, and the local Party Departments have not issued the same instructions to all of them. State policies inevitably suffer from a lack of unification, which is deeply disheartening. The association believes that at a time when national affairs, governance, and social problems are complex and numerous, it is hoped that the authorities will pay attention to major reforms, consider the overall situation, and not confine themselves to one corner, forgetting the environment, not being easily swayed by superficial changes, overcomplicating matters, not neglecting the major while focusing on the minor, and not going astray. Only then can politics be easily guided onto the right track, and academics will increasingly trend towards unity. The association humbly ventures to present its views, hoping that your department will understand the situation, learn from external environments, and be willing to maintain the original name of the Physicians' Association, placing them alongside lawyers, pharmacists, accountants, engineers, and architects in order to ensure consistency in governance and naming, which is truly convenient and fair. Respectfully submitted to the Central Training Department of the Chinese Kuomintang, the Ministry of Interior's Department of Health, Xu Nao-li, Chairman of the National Physicians' Association.

Reader's Letter

Announcement: Since October 22nd, this column has presented four questions for soliciting opinions, namely (1) Regarding the League of Nations, (2) Regarding boycotting Japanese goods, (3) Regarding volunteer armies, and (4) Regarding uniting hearts and minds to face the outside world. In the past month, we have received many responses. Those that have been published in this column include the opinions of Mr. Lin Yifang, Mr. Liu Boyong, Mr. Zhong Xia, and Mr. Zheng Hongsheng on boycotting Japanese goods, Mr. Qingyuan on volunteer armies, and Mr. Ding Jichan on uniting to face the outside world, all of which are of great value. In addition, there are quite a few others that could not be published due to space limitations. Now, the situation has changed drastically, the national crisis is becoming more urgent, the League of Nations negotiations have completely failed, the bitter battle in Heilongjiang Province has finally led to its fall, and the disturbances in Tianjin continue unabated. In the midst of this perilous state of the Chinese nation, mere sorrow, anxiety, and impatience are useless. Every one of our citizens should stand up, muster deep courage, and use their passionate minds to come up with a relatively appropriate plan for the major issues at hand and contribute to the authorities and the people. Now, please submit two questions as follows: (1) Japan's trampling of Heilongjiang Province and invasion of the Middle East route not only disregards our national sovereignty but also provokes Soviet Russia. According to common sense, Soviet Russia can no longer tolerate it. If it joins the war, it will replay the Russo-Japanese War of twenty-seven years ago. At that time, what attitude should our country take towards Japan and Soviet Russia? If it involves European and American countries, what should we do with each country? (2) National Government Chairman Chiang Kai-shek has decided to set off north to recover the lost territories soon. This is of course what the people of the whole country eagerly hope for. From now on, the overall situation will change dramatically. Military preparations will of course be the responsibility of the government. On the part of the people, what responsibilities should be fulfilled and what work should be done? What should be done to boycott Japanese goods and train volunteer armies? Each answer should be limited to a maximum of one thousand words, avoiding empty talk and focusing on proposing methods. This newspaper will select the best ones for disclosure and public discussion, depending on the capacity of this column. If you agree with the methods proposed by others, please also state so. Please include your full name, gender, age, occupation, or place of study, and native place, attach communication stamps, and a corresponding amount of postage stamps. Those that cannot be published in the newspaper will be informed by letter. As for the three questions of education, occupation, and marriage, they will still be handled according to the existing regulations. Respectfully announced.

Mr. Luo Tingguang's Message (Agrees with Mr. Lu's proposal to punish corruption): Corrupt officials harm the country and the people, which has been the same throughout history. It is painful to talk about. Recently, there has been a great promotion of transforming the government into a clean and honest one. It is not difficult to say, but it is difficult to do. Now that the national crisis is approaching, the whole country is indignant, but I have not heard of anyone who is determined to save the country. Once the enemy troops arrive, life will not be guaranteed, what about property? On the one hand, we criticize corruption, and on the other hand, we must advocate that the wealthy donate. As for punishing corruption, we must first rely on the judiciary, eliminate long-standing practices, and be impartial. Knowing that someone is corrupt, do we dare to come out and testify? This is also an important question. There is a saying, "The madman is afraid of the cat, and the mice propose to bell the cat's ear. When they hear the alarm, they run away." The mice applauded in agreement, but when they proposed who would dare to bell the cat, everyone was dumbfounded. The so-called punishing corruption is the same. Mr. Zhang and Mr. Lu were able to see this, and I also fully agree, but no one dares to come out and testify. The Kuomintang has supervisory committees and supervisory courts. Why not exercise their powers in practice? Cat, cat, mouse, mouse!

Shanghai Market

Market News 225

The Great China Rubber Factory declares that this factory was established by Xue Fuji, Wu Zhesheng, Yu Xingben, and others who have studied industrial arts in Japan for many years. Since the launch of their products in 1928, they have manufactured no fewer than 20 types of Shuang Qian brand rubber galoshes for men and women, running shoes, sports shoes, and rain shoes. They are all inexpensive and of good quality, surpassing imported goods, and are deeply appreciated and adopted by patriotic compatriots. They are a rare factory in the Chinese rubber industry. They have received dozens of awards and certifications from the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce, the current Ministry of Industry, and various competitions at home and abroad. They have also been promoted and certified by national goods organizations, so their business is very developed. Recently, since there is no domestic manufacturing of raw materials for the rubber industry, they are planning to establish the Great China Calcium Factory on Xieqiao Road in western Shanghai to manufacture calcium carbonate, which is a basic industrial raw material. The daily output of calcium carbonate is four tons, which is only enough for their own use this year. It is expected that there will be a large output in January next year, which will be used to supply the domestic goods industry, and so on.

Social News

Marshal Foch 226

European War Diary · Translated by Gu Ang Ruo

November 11th: I issued orders to all army commanders to instruct them to occupy the retreating areas of the enemy troops. November 17th: The Allied forces crossed the enemy's defense lines at the time of the armistice. 30th: The Allied forces recovered all the estimated areas (France, Belgium, Luxembourg, and Alsace-Lorraine). I entered Metz on the 25th and arrived in Strasbourg on the 26th.

At this time, I was preparing to occupy the Rhineland. I divided the Rhine into four zones: Mainz, Koblenz, Cologne, and Ellenz. I appointed the commanders of the French, American, British, and Belgian armies to occupy them separately. In principle, each zone was occupied by the troops of one country. As for the bridgeheads and the left bank of the Rhine from the Cologne bridgehead to the Dutch border, they were occupied by garrisons jointly compiled by the Allied forces of several countries to maintain the nature of the Allied occupation.

The total number of Allied troops occupying the Rhine, including the front line and reserves, was 40 infantry divisions and 5 cavalry divisions, and the military expenses were borne by the German government.

In fact, the troops estimating the bridgeheads could not completely preserve the joint nature. French troops originally co-garrisoned the Cologne bridgehead. Later, when French troops were temporarily transferred to the Belgian area near Ellenz, it was completely garrisoned by British troops.

December 1st: Allied forces entered German territory. 9th: Arrived at the Rhine. 13th: Crossed the river. 17th: The bridgehead was completely occupied. From then on, the Allied forces garrisoned the Rhine. The defeated German army could no longer move and was subject to the disposal of the Allied governments and peace treaties.

Although the world is eager for the early completion of the peace treaty, the delay in negotiations is inevitable. President Wilson was slow to arrive in France, the scope of the issues to be resolved was vast, and coordination within the Alliance was necessary in advance. All of these factors made the peace treaty have to be extended. The treaty was drafted after four months of work and accepted by Germany after another five months.

The armistice treaty signed in Le Forest was valid for only 36 days, and it expired on December 17th. At that time, the Allied plenipotentiaries began to arrive in Paris one after another. Therefore, the armistice treaty of November 11th had to be renewed. On December 12th and 13th, 1918, negotiations were held again. The former representatives met again in the original car in Le Forest and formed the following agreement:

(1) The validity period of the armistice treaty is extended by one month, until January 17th, 1919.

(2) The Supreme Commander of the Allied Forces reserves the right to occupy the neutral area on the right bank of the Rhine from the Cologne bridgehead to the Dutch border. (To be continued)
